<Author>DaKine1
<Content>Westin in the way to go I did my research so knew what to expect both good and bad. Most of the bad stuff did not really apply to me like the sink and mirror situation. When I first arrived at the hotel via Super Shuttle, I was dropped off at the corner. I had one bag and my back pack. I entered the ground floor lobby area through a turnstile doorway which was kind of tricky with luggage. I proceeded to the reception desk and checked in. I was offered a room upgrade on the top floor with an outstanding view of downtown and the Empire State Building. I could not ask for more. The room had all the usual Westin things like Starbucks Coffee, water bottles, glassware and fully stocked minibar. The only thing that was missing was the shampoo and conditioner so I called the Service Express number and three sets were sent up within ten minutes. There are two elevator banks. Elevator bank A is from floor 2-23 and elevator bank B is from 2-45. Since my room was on the 45th floor, I had to use the second bank. The Westin Club was located on the 8th floor were they provided breakfast and evening snacks daily. This was free due to my Starwood Status. You could gain access via the Club Level category rooms which are about $100 more than the other rooms. There is only one restaurant in the hotel. I did not eat here but did have a couple of drinks at their bar. the bar tendered, Brian, was very helpful and kind. There is also another bar next to the lobby, Bar 10, that is basically an extension to the lobby. It is closed off prior to noon which only leaves the small area in front of reception for people to sit. I personally did not like this option and think that both areas should be opened to the guests at all times. I have seen this in most Westin Hotels. The people working the Bell Desk did not seem overly friendly. But than again, I am in New York where friendliness is not a norm. If you had to choose a hotel in the Times Square area, this hotel would be a very good choice. It is close to everything and yet far enough away from all the noise that you would find closer to Broadway and 7th Avenue. The immediate area around the hotel is kind of tacky, but there are some good deli's, fast food and even a nice Jazz Bar around the corner. I would definitely stay here again and recommend it for singles or families. I guess on my next trip to the city, I will have to decide between the W Times Square and this hotel.

<Author>damonandtina
<Content>Solid, but not spectacular I got a very good rate on this hotel recently for a 1-night stay. Keep in mind, that good rate is a relative term in NYC, but the rate was very fair. While there was nothing bad about my stay, this location didn't quite live up to the quality level and reputation of the fine Westin brand.On the plus side:-Great bedding, towels and amenities that are trademarks of Westin-Quiet room, with no noise bleeding through from halls.-Starbucks coffee, good in-room safe and nice quality televisions.-Polite reception by a very courteous, professional staff-Loved the double-headed showers!The minuses on this property are primarily in terms of building condition and design.-My room had a significant number of wall scratches, carpet stains, and little chips on furniture that simply didn't feel luxurious.-Some pretty hefty fees to use internet connections and weight room that discouraged me from trying either.-No robes in rooms, which is different from other Westin's I've stayed in.-a loose lamp fixture that was affixed to the wall. Again, not a life or death deal, just unbecoming a luxury business hotel.-Business center, which I only looked in, seemed incredibly crowded and squished.While I would definitely stay here again, as the beds, great location, and friendly staff make it a competent and comfortable night's stay, I just feel like this hotel can push itself a little to raise its true luxury reputation. A few new room furnishings and going through each room to make sure everything is fastened tight and all the t's are crossed would make a big difference.

Here we were able to help ourselves to complimentary tasty hors d'oeuvres and soft drinks. we could also have beer or a glass of wine for $5 (much cheaper than the bar!) We purchased a cake elsewhere and the hotel stored it overnight and then provided us with a mini fridge for her room to keep the cake chilled. They also sent up a vase for her flowers within a few minutes of asking. Easy to navigate with very friendly people to help if you are not sure. <Author>PA_FanMan
<Content>Complete Satisfaction! My family passed through New York on our way to a wedding, and we decided to spend one night in the Mid-town area to catch a Broadway show (Phantom of the Opera) to celebrate our wedding anniversary! (I know... didn't have a choice, we had to bring the kids with us...) We chose the Westin NY at Times Square mostly bacause of the overwhelming number of positive reviews at this site!Well, let me tell ya, they were well deserved, and I'll add our vote to the list! We had an amazingly satisfying experience! We do have a couple of nit-picks, which I will go into later, but they were insignificant in comparison to our overall positive impression of the hotel and its services.The hotel is ideally located for anyone who plans to visit Times Square and/or catch a Broadway show while in NY! (Is there any tourist/visitor who doesn't fit this profile?!) It's a small city block away from several major Broadway theaters, and one large block away from Times Square...close enough for an easy short stroll, even in a drizzle like we had, and far enough away to not be affected by the bright lights and loud noises! I think it took us 3 minutes to walk from the Westin to the theater for Phantom. Also, we had a rental car, but for guests who don't, there's a subway station right next to the hotel, and the Port Authority is 1 small block away! It can't get any more convenient!When I made our reservation, I had requested an early check-in and a room with 2 beds. So, upon our arrival in NY, I called the front desk to check on the room availability and was very pleasantly surprised that they had upgraded us to a corner deluxe king room!! Unfortunately, we couldn't take advantage of it because it only had 1 king bed... (It was my fault, I didn't change the default 1 Adult when I made the reservation.) But, alas, the front desk clerk quickly found a room with 2 beds for us. The room wasn't cleaned yet, so we drove to the TKTS office to pick up our show tickets and had lunch before calling the hotel again. This time our room was ready! Even with the room change, we were still able to check-in about an hour before the standard 3 pm check-in, so it was early, just not as early as we had hoped. But, the front desk lady was very friendly and helpful in rearranging our rooms and apologizing for the delay!When we finally drove up to the hotel -- my first nit-pick -- none of the door men were friendly. They were efficient in unloading our car and welcomed us to the hotel, but it was spoken like a recording without warmth or even a smile. But everyone else at the hotel during our short stay were friendly, courteous and helpful! In fact, when we found out my daughter left her doll on the car, the bell boy, who was busy unloading luggages in our room, quickly called downstairs. Unfortunately, our car had already been driven away to an independent parking garage a block away. If we were to ask the garage to return the car, they would've charged us another $40 parking fee again!! So, the bell boy volunteered to show me the location of the garage. Thankfully, I was able to retrieve that #%@ing doll before all hell broke loose...Our room was located on the 40th floor with a huge window facing toward the Times Square direction!! What an amazing view of the city skyline!! We can even see the pedestrians and the neon lights of Times Square in between the buildings. But, it was surprisingly quiet because we're so high up. The street noises were very muffled and barely audible. As my wife said, we couldn't have asked for a better room location!!The room itself was very clean, modernly decorated and furnished. It was very spacious by NY standard. Even with kids and luggages, we didn't feel cramped. My wife loved the iPod dock on the stereo alarm unit! There is a big LCD TV, but we didn't try it because of our short stay and the Phantom show. Last, but not least, the 2 Westin Heavenly beds were soooooo comfortable that we just had to order one yesterday after we got back home!!!The bathroom was highly functional and roomy as well! My kids loved the 2 sprayer shower head! They thought it was the neatest thing. But, that brings up my 2nd nit-pick. The counter space in the bathroom was too limited and too shallow. My kids accidently tipped a bottle of lotion on the counter, and it fell into the toilet below. As many of you know how young kids are, sometimes they don't flush... Let's just say, it wasn't pleasant...Oh, the biggest surprise of our stay was the room service delivered a complementary bottle of champagne and 5 chocolate covered strawberries to help celebrate our anniversary!!! WOW! We were shocked!! My wife and I had to pick our jaws up from the floor when we found out!! Afterwards, we were giddy with that generous and considerate gesture!! (or, maybe it was the champagne that made us giddy...)Oh, oh, to top it off, I got an email from the hotel customer service apologizing for mixing up our room and not having it ready when we arrived into NY. As a gesture of their concern, they have credit my Starwood account with 5,000 points!! All I can say is what else can a hotel guest expect and ask for?!!! It's been one incredible experience of exceptional customer service! I must take my hat off to Maryanne, Westin's hotel manager, who have made our stay so special and memorable! I know where my family will stay in our future visits to NYC!!

I was a solo travelerand my room rate was $429 per night plus tax, so for onlytwo nights my cost was just over $1000! The internet chargeis about $18 per night, or you can pay as you go in their business center off the lobby starting at $6.95 for 15 minutes.If you like being in the middle of the craziness, just one block from Times Square and one block from the Port Authority, then this hotel is for you. The hotel restaurant, Shula's, is famous for their steak (minimum $55) and also serves an expensivebreakfast and lunch. Their are plenty of reasonably priced cafes and walk in restaurants (Cafe Europa, Ben  Jerry's) nearby.I also stayed at the Hilton Mid-town, 1335 Ave of the Americas,during this trip, and I believe it is a better value than the Westin($100 cheaper per night, great location, better service, beautifulrooms on the 33rd floor, wonderful quality inside air for a city hotel).

<Author>marblehead_prospects
<Content>Best in Times Square I've stayed at this hotel so many times I can't even count. And every time I do I'm not disappointed. The bathrooms are very clean, modern, and contemporary and I absolutely love the heavenly shower.The location is also ideal being just a block away from the middle of everything in Times Square but equally conveniently located less than a block from the Port Authority bus terminal and right across the street from the entrance to the Subway. No matter how you come into the city it's easy to get to the Westin via public transportation.I also happen to love the cocktail bar off of the lobby. Every once and awhile you can get a room here for $199/night-- which is a bargain for the area. I probably wouldn't ever pay over $299 to stay here (or anywhere for that matter) but when I see a great rate pop-up I'm always first to snatch it up. Overall I can't see one thing to fault in this hotel. Every time I try another hotel in the area I'm reminded of why I love this one so much. I will definitely be coming back again and again.

<Author>traveling_esquire
<Content>Tranquility in the middle of the Manhattan Jungle I stayed one Saturday night at Westin Times Square with my sister and mom for my sister's 30th birthday. I chose this hotel because the Hilton was not available, and we needed to stay somewhere close to both Port Authority terminal and the Schoenfeld theatre for our show that evening. We arrived prior to noon and our room was not available. We left our bags with the bellman, left the hotel, and returned after 3:00pm, the hotel's check-in time. There was somewhat of a delay in getting our room, with the front desk clerk needing to check with a supervisor, but ultimately we were given a room with 2 double beds on a high floor overlooking 8th avenue, as I had requested in my initial reservation (I am a Starwood Preferred Guest member). The room was not as small as I had expected. The bathroom had a tub/shower combo, small sink and commode, closed with a frosted pocket door. The closet contained the coffee maker, fridge and safe. The two double beds had a single nightstand between, but there was room for a desk, chair and lounge chair as well. Flat screen TV. I love the Westin's heavenly bed, and we were able to get a good night's rest. Street noise was minimal despite being on the Port Authority side of the building. We were high enough up to overlook the river and New Jersey. It was peaceful to look out over the city on Sunday morning. The window in the room actually opened for those of you who like fresh, city air. Overall the room was neat and clean. On par with Westin standards. The lobby was in classic Westin decor -- peaceful tones, spotlessly clean, pleasant scent and comfortable seating. Our guest room was pleasantly decorated in Westin's new modern look. Traveler's pictures accurately depict it. Service was good. I asked for a birthday cake for my sister and they delivered it when we returned from the show. Despite the wait, check-in and check-out were smooth. I had to correct the room rate at check-out, but this was done with pleasantly and without incident. Our rate included in-room breakfast, which was delicious, fresh and up to Westin's standards. Bell staff were eager to help and hail a cab. Overall, the hotel had the tranquil, upscale ambience makes you feel relaxed and welcomed the minute you enter the hotel. I would choose this hotel again for my Manhattan hotel needs and would recommend it without hesitation.

<Author>mdean09
<Content>Peaceful Stay in a Hectic Location My girlfriend and I have just returned from a 5 night stay at the Westin at Times Square and cannot complain about the service received or the room itself.Reception Staff - very helpful indeed. For all those visitors using Travellers Cheques, they do not charge to exchange them.Room - Asked for a high room with a view and although not looking at any stand-out feature of NYC, the view was good. The room and bathroom was always clean and tidy. The bed is very comfortable after a long hard day walking and we found there was adequate bathroom space for toiletries, etc. We were advised the minibar was sensitive to movement so don't be too tempted to see what is in there. If travelling from Europe, dont take your hairdryer as they are not as powerful when used in the US plug sockets (as my girlfriend found out!).Only downside was the constant reminder for tips from the baggage handlers and the guys on the front door. We appreciate they make their wages up with tips but do not think the constant reminders are required. Not the best location for food - unless you want fast food but for breakfast there are plenty of coffee shops and other bakeries selling croissants, muffins, etc. (PAX opposite Madame Tussauds is good).If getting a yellow cab back to the hotel, just tell them near the Port Authority Building as not one taxi driver knew where the Westin was!Trip Tips - Do Top Of The Rock at dusk and watch the sunset (we would advise you give it a day or two (if you can) just so you can work out what time the sun sets and then go up after you know). The Grayline bus tours were good (uptown, downtown and the night tour) but felt it became a broadway audition from the 'wannabe actor' guides at times rather than them telling you points of interest (although we did get one older guide who was very informative) and again with the constant tip reminders. We would advise you to prebook your tickets for the Statue of Liberty and get there early to avoid the queues. If there are any students in your party take your student cards if you are going to any of the museums for a slight discount. Use the subway as its fast, cheap and not as scary as you may think. Used Grand Central to get to Bloomingdales and the Brooklyn bridge and both stops bring you out right next to them.Would stay at the hotel again.

Anyway, besides the price, I have absolutely no regrets about staying at the Westin. Location: Between 7th and 8th Avenues and 42nd and 43rd Streets. You are in the center of everything! Every subway line stops within a 1/2 block of the hotel. Times Square is within a block. You have the option of exiting/entering on 42nd or 43rd...If you're going on a walk to times square, etc. you can enter/exit on 42nd and be in the center of the action. If you need a cab with a lot less hassle, exit on 43rd and the bellman can get for you without dealing with all of the traffic/people of times square. There are drug stores within a block, restaurants line every street (the 24 hour McD's came in handy), two movie theaters (one in the hotel and one across the street on 42nd), Madame Tussaud's, and Ripley's are across the street. Friends we traveled with stayed near the UN and in Murray Hill. No matter where we were traveling for the day, we always had to start out in Times Square. So, it took us 2 minutes to get to the meeting place, they had to take cabs, buses, or very long walks.Hotel cleanliness, amenities: There is a Shula's Steakhouse and bar on the property...I didn't try either so I can't give a review on them. However, it was nice having the option. The room itself was extremely clean and exactly as pictured on the websites I researched before booking. We had a view of the Hudson River. The windows are tinted so you are not bothered by blazing sunrises/sunsets. We were on the 43rd floor and coincidentally there was an ice machine on our floor that was very convenient. The bedding and shower were fantastic! I've been in a number of hotels that offer their products for sale...this is one of the first I actually browsed through for pricing and purchase details. Amazingly, the prices weren't out of this world...I would definitely consider purchasing the double shower head and comforter/duvet, etc. We had occassion to speak with the concierge--we had to leave messages as to our requests and we received return phone calls or the information requested was printed and slipped under our door..AWESOME! The front desk clerk that handled both our check-in and check-out was friendly and recognized/thanked us for being Starwood members and asked if I had any questions/requests. Upon checking out we checked our baggage with the bell desk--we left our luggage with them for several hours while we went to explore Central Park and Midtown Comics before our flight home. Both drop off and pick up of our bags was smooth as silk and not to mention convenient. The only improvement I'd make to the hotel might be a pool but, who knows if we would even have time to enjoy it...not a deal breaker. Bottom line, I would definitely stay here again and look forward to doing so very soon.

<Author>EuroLondon
<Content>Pretty alright Stayed here in May for a few nights, after a business trip spent in the Sofitel. The Westin is quite touristy, but I thought it was pretty good for the money- only $320 per night for a deluxe room. A bargain for New York. Check in took a while- big queue in the lobby, but staff were friendly. Had a room on the 40th floor with a very decent view. Would recommend that people try to book a room on a high floor- even on the 40th, you could hear a little noise from the street, which was fine, but I suspect rooms on lower floors might be a bit noisy. The bedrooms feel a bit clinical- no warm wood tones here. Lots of white and grey surfaces, mixed with very dark wood. Sort of slate and stainless steel in the bathroom. Really comfortable mattress. Nice flatscreen tv. Room size wasn't massive, but definitely fine for one person. The rooms on higher floors are labelled as newly renovated. However, because it is such a busy hotel, I suspect these new rooms won't look new for very long. Some very minor signs of wear and tear. Also suspect the non-renovated rooms might not be very nice. Soundproofing in the room was alright. Not as good as the Sofitel, but miles better than the Grand Hyatt's paper-thin walls. There's a gym here, kind of small. Went to have a look around- a few machines, a bench, some free weights and mats. The hotel guide said there was a $10 charge- but I'm not sure if they actually make people pay. Instead I walked up a few blocks to W 55th Street and bought a day pass to somewhere called Club H- fantastic gym. Really clean, well equipped, loads of free weights and machines, plus a smoothie bar. Much better option if you want a decent workout- $25 but worth it if you are into the gym.Location is cheesy, but handy. Would definitely recommend the Westin for anyone going to New York for a holiday.

Location? Well, what's there to say? The Westin on Time Square says just that: the buzzing Time Square in front of it. I think I would rather go to a little more 'authentic' in a more quiet neighborhood, possibly a BB.... The Westin - certainly not a bad choice, and if you want to be on the safe side, check in a hotel that appears to be safe, clean, central, etc. Be prepared to avoid the hotel options in regards to food unless you don't mind paying $30 for a chicken sandwich. <Author>WDWDolphinFan
<Content>Pros and Cons, But Very Touristy! I stayed at the Westin on a recent business trip. The location would be a plus for trips focused on the theaters, and may well be excellent for families sightseeing in New York, but I found the location a big drawback. The area around the hotel is packed with tourists, chain restaurants, and garish signs - a very different atmosphere than comparable mid-town hotels outside the Times Square area. I can see that having affordable restaurants that appeal to kids and teenagers would be a big plus for family trips, but the atmosphere in the surrounding area was not the New York I knew from many prior trips.  On the other hand, standard rooms here are a bit larger than at many other New York hotels, with much better views. The prevalence of rooms with good views is the hotel's biggest draw. The bathrooms are depressing, though - clearly meant to be someone's idea of modern, but instead just look like what you'd expect to find in a public train station. In what seems to be an trend these days, the door to the bathroom is glass (at least this one is rather opaque), making it almost impossible for someone to use the bathroom at night or before sunrise without the light waking a companion.  If this hotel were in a different location, I would definitely be back - the hotel is very nice (except for those regrettable bathrooms), with views that are both good and rare for New York. For families heading to New York to sightsee, though, this would be a great choice.

<Author>Uppy
<Content>A Wonderful, Lovely Stay at the Westin Our rooms were booked using Priceline less than a week before our stay. Our 2 night Monday to Wednesday stay, May 12-14, at the Westin went well. There was no way I could pay rack rates of $500 a night so without Priceline our spur of the moment, side trip to New York from Washington D.C. would not have happened. My tired, aching feet were happy our Priceline bid landed us at the Westin-Times Square.When I called to confirm our reservation, at check in and when we checked out no mention was made of Priceline. All that was noted was that the room was prepaid. I was asked for a photo ID at check in and a credit card for incidentals. Westin staff were all cordial and helpful. I saw no children other than ours at the hotel during our stay. Every Westin staff person we ran into welcomed the kids. They were made to feel really special, complimented and treated like little princesses. I noted we were traveling with 3 young children and needed rooms next door to each other when I called to confirm. I was actually assigned adjoining rooms, exactly what we wanted. The standard Westin-Times Square (a bit confusing because Westin-New York is on hotel signs) room has 2 double beds so this worked great for us. I do remember looking out the window at some point and the view was nothing special. A view was not important as what little time we spent in the room we were asleep or getting dressed so the shades were drawn. A shame really because the room had wall to wall windows. There were both shades and black out curtains at the windows. The trademark Westin beds were as marketed, heavenly.Room size seemed normal with ample room between the beds and the walls. I liked the padded bench to sit on or to put suitcases on that was next to the dresser. We lived out of our suitcase so did not use the dresser drawers. If 4 people are in the room drawer space will be tight. The bathroom had a pocket door and an itty bitty sink but was as spacious as most hotel bathrooms with excellent water pressure. One white terry cloth robe and one bottle each of shampoo, conditioner, lotion, mouth wash with 2 small bars of soap stocked the bathroom. If I cared or was the nitpicking sort I guess I could complain that no shower cap was provided. The towels were large and 4 complete sets per room were provided. I saw one woman in the elevator carrying a cellophane wrapped toothbrush with a 1 inch tube of toothpaste so I assume extra hygiene products were available upon request. The room was clean and all rooms were non smoking. At one point during the evening I was sure I smelled cigarette smoke. I'm not sure how the nonsmoking rule is enforced. There was a large flat screen TV, a safe, iron, coffee maker, ice bucket, glasses and disposable cups, IPOD dock with radio and alarm clock in the room but no refrigerator with high priced snacks. If you can't find something look in the closet everything, even the coffee maker, was hidden behind the sliding door. We heard the occasional siren during the night but no other city noise. Once the door was closed I heard no hall noise or sounds from neighboring rooms. Walking down the hallway, I could hear the TVs from other rooms. I'm not one for decor but I think modern best describes the rooms. Not exactly my cup of tea but black, orangy gold and stainless steel were what stuck with me along with the all white heavenly beds. We arrived by train at Penn Station (about 5 minutes and $6.25 by taxi to the Westin) so I have no idea what parking was like or the cost. I found using busses or the subway to get around was not particularly easy, inexpensive or fast. If they could be found the Transit employees were not at all helpful in navigating the system so we relied on our feet. The Times Square crowds were not too bad during the day but at night the sidewalks were so crowded it was difficult to walk. On a positive note this made me feel quite safe walking with kids (holding hands in a chain) out late after taking in a couple of Broadway shows. We saw Phantom at the Majestic Theater less than a 2 minute walk from the Westin. Our Tuesday night show was at the Longacre on 49th between 8th and Broadway. Through the slooow evening crowds this was about a 15 minute walk.The Westin was a 5 to 7 minute stroll to the Marriott Marquis where the TKTS discount ticket booth is temporarily located. This was important because I had not booked any theater tickets and relied on TKTS for tickets for both nights. In fact we stopped and purchased tickets for our first night before checking into the Westin. The Westin's location made it easy to plan our sight seeing around the TKTS booths hours, allowing one adult to stand in line while the other took the kids back to the hotel to rest and for snacks. The TKTS line moved quickly. On Monday I got in line at 3:07 and had tickets at 3:48. On Tuesday we got in the play only line at 2:00 and had tickets to our show of choice in 15 minutes. I've been told this is common early in the week but one should arrive at the booth earlier later in the week and on weekends. On our last day at the Westin I asked for a late check out but it was not available. We checked out at noon and were able to leave our bags with the bellman and get in a full day of sight seeing. I was told as long as we were back to pick up our bags by midnight we would be fine. We of course got back well before midnight. The bellman got us a taxi with no waiting and we were off. The Westin was an excellent hotel at any price and a dream come true at Priceline rates.

There was a large LCD television, Ipod clock radio alarm with docking station for your Ipod, hairdryer, safe, mini bar and all the other usual hotel comforts. Most surprising though was the fact that everything worked, nothing looked worn out, shabby or of poor quality. In fact, there was nothing to complain about. Being so high up also meant that we got no noise problems!Though on a high floor, the elevators are plenty and incredibly fast, only a few seconds to the ground. It is also on the doorstep of the theatre district, which means you can have a great night out, have something to eat and still be within a short distance of the hotel.So, would definitely choose the Westin at Times Square again for our next trip!

The room was cleaned immaculately each day.The location of the hotel is great - it's one block off Times Square but it's within walking distance of a lot of the sights - we walked to Macy's and the Empire State Building in about 20 mins. We walked to Central Park in about 30 mins. I would thoroughly recommend this hotel to visitors to New York. For comfort and quality, it represents good value for money.

<Author>JanJanVanMan
<Content>Excellent with a couple of hiccoughs To be fair, this is a good hotel. We had an club level room and loved having the Apple computer and free internet access. It was extremely useful.We chose to stay here following reading a number of reviews on this web-site. The room was a good size and it was tastefully decorated. It was useful having breakfast in the club room especially with little ones. The location was good too. I had no problems with the location. Some people mentioned that Times Square would be a nightmare for driving because of the one way system. We had a navigation system in the rental car (an absolute must for going to NYC) and we didn't get lost once. Toys R Us with its ferris wheel is very close and the kids enjoyed the ride.On the negative side, we arrived at about 3.00 and the lobby was heaving so it took us about 30 minutes to check in. If you have a car parked at the hotel, do remember to get the reception to stamp your ticket and also to hand over the porter/bell hop ticket so that your luggage is delivered to your room. I would have given this hotel a much higher rating if we didn't have a problem with the room cleaning. Having been out all day, we returned to our room to find that it still wasn't made up. I had left our dirty laundry in the appropriate bag on our door, as the laundry sheet advised that laundry to be done the following day should be outside your hotel room by 9.00 in the morning. I dutifully did this, but did not call reception to ask someone to pick the laundry up. The maid therefore saw the laundry on the door and decided not to clean the room. The maid gave me real attitude when I asked her why she hadn't cleaned the room and if she could do it now. I was quite surprised by how rude she actually was! I reported this to the concierge and to be fair the next day the cleaning was done quickly and efficiently. Lesson learned: if you want trays picked up, laundry picked up or anything else done - simply call the express phone number on the phone and don't hang around waiting for things to happen because they won't!Finally, we took advantage of the hotel doctor because my son had developed an ear infection and was in a good deal of pain. I should stress that there isn't a hotel doctor, but a number the hotel gives you for an on-call doctor who will come to your hotel room. The doctor called to understand the age of the patient and the problem before arriving laden with all the correct medications, antibiotics, drops, injection etc. It was a little OTT but we were flying in 36 hours and I didn't want to risk a problem. I was fairly impressed by the doctor's conscientiousness until I got the bill which was for $510. I almost fainted! Worse, I had to pay the doctor in cash as she wouldn't take any cards. Fortunately, there is an ATM in the lobby, but I did feel a bit like a pimp paying her by the elevators. Our insurance wouldn't cover the bill when we got back home because the doctor was outside of our health care network. Just beware of this in advance and check that you are covered should the need arise!Another plus (I thought) was the food. The room service menu was unusually good, varied and HEALTHY! The children's menu was also a refreshing change to the norm. I was impressed.

<Author>BG3505
<Content>Nice hotel We stayed at Westin over MLK weekend with a group that included two children under 6 and a teenager. The location was great--easy to walk to lots of attractions. The beds and shower are as advertised---heavenly. We did have a few minor service issues (no bell person to help us with our 5 suitcases when we arrived, our corner room was not available when we arrived, no mini bar price list in the room) but these issues were dealt with quickly and apologetically by the staff. The only person who was not helpful was the Saturday morning female concierge who would barely give us any information--we had to ask for a map, ask for her to show us where we were going on the map, ask her about tours and then she did not even mention that they have a tour desk to help with those. But the other concierge people were great--definitely use them to get your dinner reservations. A few tips:-go to hotel website to look for deals--we booked a deal that was stay 2 nights, 3d night free. <Author>ltlor
<Content>Not terrible, but not great for a Westin My husband and I stayed at the Westin for one night over MLK weekend. What is good is that it is centrally located for the theater, and other times square activities, that area is also good for picking up lines that allow for good subway connections. There are two stations really very close to the hotel that will allow you to get uptown - downtown very quickly without too much confusion.For a Westin, not so great. I thought that it was a bit tired granted we did get a cheap for new york rate from Travelzoo but it still did not meet what I have experienced in other Westins. It is still not a bad place to stay - it's a nice hotel, very modern nice bathroom and yes the heavenly bed was great. So I would recommend it - I just want folks to know this is just a step above a comfort inn - not what you would normally expect from a Westin.The worst and I mean worst part about the location - the noise. It is NYC so I expected traffic etc...but on Saturday night in NYC in the Times Sq area it is LOUD. This hotel is not sound proofed or even close to it. We were on the 10th floor - and it sounded like I was sleeping on the street level right next to the people walking on the street and talking and the police cars all night! That really was bad. Not a show stopper for some but it also can be overcome by others if planned for so my recommendation to combat this issue and bring earplugs. With some earplugs you can block out the sound and get a great nights sleep. The hotel should really put white noise machines in the room, or those sleep sound machines. I would recommend this hotel if you get a deal - do not pay the published rates - shop around - and do not pay more than 200.00 tops. It is not worth more than that - it's really not even worth that but finding less in NYC is not easy.

<Author>TheTravelJunkie
<Content>Westin was good, but not great. Our overall stay at the Westin-TS was good. You will have a clean comfortable room with very professional staff to assist you.The Good:From the moment we arrived, we were met with excellent customer service. All employees- doormen, front desk staff, concierge were friendly and helpful during our stay. Our room (3908) was ready for early check-in when we arrived at 1:30pm on a Saturday. The average size room had wonderfully large windows that could be cracked for fresh air and had a very nice view of the Hudson during the day and city lights at night. The room had two fluffy queen beds with lots of pillows, a night stand in between with cordless phone and ipod ready radio. There was one fabric chair next to the window and one desk chair at the shelf desk that had work space with computer hook-ups on one end and the flat screen t.v. on the other. There was also an attached cushioned bench and then a space for the luggage stand. Coffee maker was in the closet-hmmm?with Starbucks coffee packs, condiments.Room was cleaned in a timely manner with plenty of towels, etc replaced. Doormen eagerly hailed taxi/gave directions. Security at night asked for hotel key before allowing entry up the escalators which was welcomed. Subway entry was close with connections everywhere. Starbucks right across the street had shorter lines than the one down the block at Times Square. Duane Read drug store across the street was handy for magazines and aspirin. Close to theaters and restaurant row.The Not So Good:The hotel is 2 blocks FROM Times Square. Not a problem if you know, but my mother was under the assumption that we were going to be walking out of our hotel door and be in Times Square. Also, not much to look at immediately around the hotel..electronic shops, drug store, and we didn't really care to walk out each night to see neon light for the adult entertainment club with live action on the opposite corner.  The hotel has an odd layout...you enter the hotel at street level and then take an escalator up one flight to check-in. Because the lobby area is not connected to any outside walls it has a dark feel to it, everything is muted tones-nice-but, it feels very much like a business hotel. Messages for where seminars are meeting, people walking around with name tags( like my mom)/working on laptops...not a leisure or peaceful ambiance. The two elevator halls are dark and around a corner. The tiny sundries shop is appreciated but, stuck into a corner with small inventory. The room met our needs-the view and comfy beds saved it! But, even on the 39th floor, we could here fire engines coming and going all day/night. The bathroom is very small with little counter space and had an institutional feel with the stainless bowl sink and black slate tile-which had mildew growing all along the base where the white tub met the tile. Because there is no mirror in the bedroom-we had to choose either being cramped/straddle the commode or delayed by waiting for each other to take turns with make-up/hair drying, showering, etc. They really need to add a mirror in the bedroom for make-up application, dressing, etc so that one person can be showering while another can finish getting ready in the bedroom. Appreciate the fluffy robe in the bathroom (we wondered with 2 queens-why not two robes? oh-well)We had no problems during our stay and chose this hotel because our seminar was located here. If returning for leisure, I will choose a hotel that has more of a laid back atmosphere.

We just made it a habit every night to put the DND sign on the door in case we had a late start the next morning.New York at New Year is CHAOS! Given the hotel was a max capacity we felt they remained on top of things and we never felt the service level was compromised. (I've never seen so many people in a hotel as I did on New Years Eve!!!) Even if you don't stay at the Westin, you must eat at Shula's Steak House within as it was fabulous (but if you want the best, then it is filet mignon at Jordan's at Grand Central Station every time!!)

<Author>linda528
<Content>Happily Surprised My husband and I recently settled on the Westin Times Sqaure, as it was the only hotel left in NYC where I could use my Starwood points. We are very glad we did. Although I've generally shunned Times Square on visits back to NYC, we had a great time. The hotel itself is well-located on 43d and Eighth Avenue, close to numerous theatres as well as Hell's Kitchen and within easy walking distance of Madison Avenue shopping. The hotel lobby was bustling but the staff efficient--as a Starwood gold member, we received a complimentary upgrade to a deluxe king corner room on the 28th floor -- absolutely fabulous room with flat screen TV, wonderful bed, iHome, and gorgeous corner room views of the city. The bathroom was great too--never wanted to get out of the double-headed shower. I can't comment on the lower rooms and street noise, but we couldn't hear a thing in our lovely room. A couple of small quibbles: the concierge was snotty and could not seem to believe we had arrived on Christmas night without a dinner reservation. We asked if she could recommend any nearby Asian food andshe told us everything was likely booked and lamely offered to call a place I'd never heard of on the upper east side (not close) that wasprobably booked. We said no thanks and walked over to Ninth Avenue (a block away!), where we found a number of Asian places serving dinner, no reservations required. <Author>jonahleon
<Content>A Solid Choice in New York The Westin at Times Square is a good hotel choice, especially if you can get a deal like we did for $210 a night during the December holiday season (be sure to visit both the starwood website and the hotel's separate website for the best rates; we booked in October). The lights gave off a greenish-yellow hue in the room which was a bit odd. The hotel is a block away from the subway, which is very convenient. All in all, I think most people come to New York to be in the city and experience things other than their hotel. And, if you fall into that camp, this hotel will be a very nice respite for the end of a busy day of siteseeing.

<Author>theseatsaretooclose
<Content>Great central location Gone are the days when Times Square and seedy could be said in the same sentence. Unless of course you are discussing how it's not seedy anymore. The Westin is but one of several new properties that grace the Times Square and theater district. It's location is ideal for people coming into the Port Authority building by bus from Newark or other locales. As well it has good subway access below it, for quick trips to the Village or uptown to Central Park. The rooms are standard Westin fare. Not as cutting edge as the W, but nice with very comfortable beds and bedding. The television had a solid channel selection with some premium channels. However, two problems with this hotel are the shower and curtains/window frames. The shower had the really annoying problem of losing water pressure frequently, only to then have a torrent of scalding water rush through, followed by an equally disturbing cold water bath. Nothing bothers me more than a bad shower. It just ruins the start of any day and a brand new hotel has no excuse. Also the metal exterior of the hotel acts as a tuning fork, as it brings in the various sounds from the rooms next door. A neighbor closing his/her curtains is so loud, you almost think its your curtains being closed. Overall though, it is still a very nice hotel, but at that price and in that city, there are so many other choices that may be better.

<Author>Ozi_Traveller
<Content>Lousy Club Room How can this property be rated as a Category 6 by Starwood?I have stayed in Starwood properties on over 30 occasions this year, and have been in the top tier of their frequent stayer program for more than 10 years now.This is one of the most over-rated properties I have stayed in. The foyer and checkin staff met expectations - it looked good, and the staff were helpful, polite, and very friendly. The room was just okay. It was more consistent with a Category 3-4 hotel - very basic furnishings, bland decor, poor quality window covers, and not that much better than an average to superior motel (some Holiday Inn Express properties have better looking rooms).The view was quite poor. The higher floors get great views from 3 sides only - so 'bad luck' if they allocate you a room on the side looking towards time square, as you can't see much past the buildings next door!! Maybe a higher floor would have helped, but we were on a floor in the high 20's.Our biggest problem was the Club room at breakfast and evening drinks time. They had clearly booked more people than the space, amenities, food, drinks, and staff could cope with. At breakfast time we had to cue for 20 minutes for each breakfast item we needed. It was mind boggling to see that they had two toasters for 50 people in the room! A long time to wait for those bagels to toast! There was insufficient seating, and we had to wait a considerable amount of time on each morning. If we stay again, we would prefer to go somewhere else for breakfast - it isn't worth the 1 hour trauma to get two bagels, juice and coffee.When I provided the duty manager with feedback on our last morning, she did apologize, informed me that it was because they had so many people booked for Easter, and offered us another breakfast in the main restaurant. A better response might have been for the hotel to manage its bookings so they could meet demand and/or increase the space for its Club amenities if it wants to cater for so many people.If you're looking for a 'reasonable' hotel, with no particular frills, in a great location - then its pretty good. If you're expecting something special - particularly for a Category 6 - then you are likely to be disappointed. If you're used to the Westin hotels of Europe, Australia and Asia - then give this a miss and try the much more stylish W at Times Square.Peter and AnnMelbourne, Australia

For an infant, the crib would've been fine. It was great having a bathroom that was big enough to help the baby take her bath without feeling crowded. The room was clean, but showed clear signs of wear and tear. Some touch up on the trim and wallpaper could resolve this. The TV and computer were great, but even though we had a slick iMac in the room there is an additional charge for Internet access. We were on the 12th floor, and the street noise still was quite intrusive. The hotel should consider replacing the double pane glass with laminated windowsto reduce street noise (especially sirens) or submit to less chic window coverings and install heavy curtains to muffle the sound. Curtains also would help with climate control, as it was cool outside and the heat in the room could barely keep the temperature up unless the fan was turned up from low to the louder medium setting regardless of how high you set the thermostat. Otherwise, the room wasalmost silent -- we never heard a door or footstep or any other sound from within the hotel.In the past we'd usually stayed at the Rihga Royal or Essex House. Both of those hotels have changed owners (and market positions) so we went with the Westin. We like the chain because we know we will like the beds and it is rather casual (although I love Ritz, etc., I don't typically shave or wear a tie on weekends, and parents don't always feel welcome with kids in some of the more upscale hotels).We'd be happy to stay here again, but it truly is in the center of themayhem of Times Square, so we may look for a quieter part of town nexttime.

We ordered room service for breakfast on one occasion and were not disappointed - it was lovely, although as with everything in New York - the portions were huge!We didn't eat at the Hotel restaurant, nor did we use any of the facilities - although we would certainly stay again...do try Budda Bar - the food and service is great and the ambience is wondeful.

<Author>bluevoter
<Content>For expense-account travelers and the wealthy The Westin is an excellent hotel if you are OK with spending $500/night for your room (including taxes) or having someone spend it on your behalf. The $500 is just for a start, though, since continental breakfast is $20, wired Internet access is $15, the exercise facility is $10, designer water in the room is $7, and even printing your airline boarding pass is $1.50. If you upgrade (higher room rate) to the Executive room, then you get a 17 iMac in the room (nice touch!), a 32 LCD TV, and access to the lounge, which includes a continental breakfast.As for the location, you are literally on top of 9 subway lines, a block from 40 movie theaters, close to the Port Authority Bus Terminal, and within walking distance of all of the Broadway theaters. If you like the activity of the Times Square neighborhood, this hotel or the nearby Hilton and Marriott is for you. However, the Millennium Broadway and the Muse (Kimpton) are not far away, and they are considerably quieter. (I've stayed in all of these hotels over the years, but personally prefer to stay on the quieter Upper West Side near Broadway and the number 1 subway line).As I'm an urban survivor by nature, I didn't mind the frequent sirens on 42nd Street or 8th Avenue, but that might be an annoyance for some visitors. On the second night of my stay, we were awakened at 4:30 AM by a fire alarm and a sequence of announcements broadcast over a speaker system into the guest rooms. After 20 minutes, we were told that it was a false alarm. From what I could tell, the hotel staff treated this event as a routine occurrence, so make sure that you bring pajamas and a robe with you for a possible room evacuation.

<Author>dgtray
<Content>First trip to NYC We spent a long weekend at the Westin Times Square Sept. 27 - 30. I used Starwood points to book the room and and we were upgraded to a Club King room. However, since we aren't platinum (only gold) we didn't have access to the loung which was a little disappointing. Our room was on the 16th floor and we had a view of 7th Ave, but we couldn't see the street since we didn't face it directly. Not a big deal since we weren't in the room that much and we didn't hear the street noise. The club room was large with a sitting area, heavenly bed, large flat screen HD TV. The bathroom was large enough, but the as many have mentioned the counter space was limited. The two headed shower was nice. The hotel staff was friendly, but we didn't really need to see them very often. We did get a map and printed our boarding passes at the concierage. Some info about the local area. The hotel is between 42nd and 43rd streets and 7th and 8th avenue. You can enter our leave the hotel on either 42nd or 43rd depending on which path you take from the lobby. If you go out the 43rd street exit you will find a drug store on 8th ave. where you can stock up on water or other things you may need for your sightseeing adventures. We ate at the Europa cafe on 43rd and the Pax Foods on 42nd for breakfast. Both are very short walks from the hotel and have decent prices. Also, the 42nd street station is right by the hotel and accessible from either exit. We were able to get a metro card for $10 with 6 rides. You are also a short walk from all of the buzz of Times Square and can join the thousands of other people walking along 7th avenue and Broadway looking at the lights, the people and shopping. We ate the first night at the Mexican restaurant outside the hotel lobby which was decent. Also, there is a Starbucks down the escalotor from the Mexican place. I almost forgot there is a movie theatre up the escalator if you were interested.I almost fogot about traveling from and to the airport. We decided to reserve a car and driver from Carmels for the trip vs. a taxi or bus service. It worked out well and the price to the hotel was $28 and from the hotel was $33. You are responsible for tolls and tip too.If you read any of my reviews you know I like to run and there is an excellent running route from the hotel. You go out the 43rd street exit and run to the 12th avenue (right by the Hudson) and there is a running/walking/biking path all the way to Battery Park. I planned to run to Central Park, but only ran one day, so I missed out on a run in the park adventure.On to the sightseeing tips. We did the following: Ground Zero, Wall Street, Brooklyn Bridge, Natural History Museum, Central Park, Empire State building, Top of the Rock, Statue of Liberty, shopping on 5th avenue, walking in Little Italy and Chinatown. If you are going to the Statue of Liberty go to the park service web site and get museum passes, so you can visit the museum and go up the first 156 steps (as high as you can go). If you don't have a pass then you can't see inside. The line for security before you board the ferry is easily 60 minutes, and if you have a museum pass then you go through security again on Liberty Island. The ferry goes from Battery Park to Liberty Island to Ellis Island and back. You can stay as long as you like on each stop and get in line for the ferry when you are ready to go (we didn't visit Ellis Island). By the way the security is probably more extensive than airport security, and you can't carry a backpack into the museum. The park service web site has information on security requirements. From the time we got in line to the time we returned on the ferry was close to 3 hours.We spent more than 3 hours at the Natural History Museum and Planetarium. There is a lot to see and some really good exhibits and shows, but I probably like the Smithsonian a little better. After the museum we tripped through Central Park and enjoyed some wonderful scenary on a beautiful Friday afternoon. By the way the subway takes you directly to the museum.It was difficult to see much at Ground Zero due to all of the construction. You can walk around the perimeter and peek through the fence, but the best view is probably from the Empire State building.The Top of the Rock trip was well worth it. The lines were short and you get some great views of the city plus a nice video show on the ceiling of the elevator on your trip up. We were only in town for a long weekend, so Little Italy and Chinatown was one area where we spent some time Saturday afternoon. It was absolutely packed with people on just about every block and if you want to shop you can find just about anything you desire.Overall we had a great time and exhausted ourselves trying to see as much as possible on the trip. Next time we will take it a little slower and limit our sightseeing trips significantly. The hotel is excellent and we felt secure wherever we went in the city.  
<Date>Oct 2, 2007

<Author>hopenm
<Content>Hit and Miss Let me start by saying that I stay at Westins often and am a starwood member. Having said that, this Westin was not up to par, especially at over $400.00 a night. First the good things:We had a great view, the a.c. kept up with the 95+ heat, the customer service manager was apologetic and helpful when we called with issues and the concierge and bell folks were very helpful. This is also a very central location and we had no trouble walking or subway-ing our way all over the city.Now the issues: We booked this hotel as part of a vacation package, so we knew we wouldn't be getting any starwood points for the price of the room. However, as I confirmed later with Starwood services, you are supposed to get points for things you purchase at the hotel - food, spa, etc. I have done this at other Westins. When we checked in I tried to give the check-in person my Starwood card so we could get points for these incidentals - she flatly refused. She said because we booked through a vacation package we got no points for anything. I tried to explain to her what I just explained here, but she would not listen and was very rude. Not the type of customer service I'm used to at Westin.Next - for some strange reason, every day we were given a new bottle of mouthwash, even though we never used it. In contrast, the shower gel, which we used up the first day, was never replaced - 4 bottles of mouthwash, no shower gel! When my husband called on the third day to ask for shower gel, they said it would be right there. 1.5 hours later I called the service manager and only then did we get shower gel (actually an entire bag of bathroom stuff we didn't ask for, including about 4 more mouthwashes - is some trying to tell me something?!?!?!)Housekeeping also left anything that wasn't put in the trash - the empty coffee supplies, the empty bottles in the shower, etc. I have never had that kind of stuff left in the room anywhere.Finally, and this is a general Westin complaint as it was also true in Boston. You can't just print the words heavenly bath on a bar of soap and think that makes it a heavenly bath. True Westins have a wonderful seperate shower and a deep soaking tub - THAT is heavenly. A regualr old shower/shallow tub combo is not heavenly and rather dissapointing after a long day of walking and looking forward to a nice soak. There should be some standard for what is and is not labeled heavenly bath.So, all in all, if I had it to do over again, with as easy as the city is to navigate, I would have found a more reasonbly priced hotel out of time square and from now on will call all Westins and ask them just what is so heavenly about their bath before I book.

<Author>joshdotcom
<Content>An honest level-headed review I have stayed in many hotels in New York and around the world. As I see it hotels can be divided into three groups: (1) hotels where you feel like you get what you pay for, (2) hotels where you feel like you had a truly special experience, and (3) hotels where you feel like you have been robbed. Now just because you spend $400 a night and a bowl of name-brand cereal costs $10 does not mean you are being robbed. A good hotel will give you the service, presentation and comfort that $400 a night and a $10 bowl of cereal warrants (e.g. some of the hotels run by St. Regis, Four Seasons, Ritz Carlton). Other hotels, like your average Holiday Inn or Best Western, give you what you pay for (a wholly average experience). The Westin at Times Square sadly fits into the third category - a hotel that is simply not worth the money you pay and will leave you feeling like you are the victim of extortion. If you do choose to stay here make sure you stay in a room ending in the number 9 - these are the best rooms and surprisingly a middle category of room type - a deluxe. Whatever you do - do not stay in a junior suite - they are small (the pictures on the website are completely misleading) and they are fairly unattractive. Why is this hotel average? The service simply does not live up to its price category. To be fair to the hotel, they try, but the hotel is simply too large to make anyone feel as if they have had a personalized experience - and at more than $500 a night (you will pay an average of about $60-$100 extra in taxes and charges above your room rate) it is simply not worth it. There are no chocolates on your bed, fresh fruit in a basket or free bottles of champagne. There is maid service once a day and they do not do anything like fold your clothes or turn down the bed at night. The room service offers four star restaurant prices with a corner deli quality of food product - the closest you an come to getting anything truly satisfying is ordering a $6 cup of Starbucks coffee. What becomes blatantly obvious at a hotel like the Westin Times Square is that the hotel is willing to trade profit for customer satisfaction - unfortunately because the hotel is on one of the busiest (and unattractive) intersections in New York it is not likely that the hotel will learn its lesson anytime soon - and what lesson is that? - that the hotel business is a service industry and nothing in a service industry is more important than a loyal customer. This hotel could not care less whether you come back - maybe that's because they know you won't. All that being said, if you are a business person who will be staying at a hotel on corporate dollar and you will be spending your days outside of the hotel and you need a central location and for the most part you want to be left alone - book a room here ending in the number 9 on a high floor and you will be happy - I promise.Yours truly,World Traveler  
<Date>Jul 25, 2007

<Author>NCG
<Content>Fabulous Room I took my daughter to New York for her 18th birthday. We stayed at this hotel from 28th June to 1st July 2007 and upgraded to a club twin. The upgrade was well worth the extra as it included a lovely continental style breakfast and we were able to get drinks and snacks in a hurry after a busy day sightseeing and shopping and with little time to spare to find a restaurant before going to the theatre. There was a wide screen television and a computer. The bathroom was also spacious and despite what other reviewers say there was adequate room beside the basin for toiletries and there was also a 3 tier trolley on which you could put sponge bags, hairdrier etc. There was only one bathrobe but we called housekeeping and a second one was brought within about ten minutes. The bath was quite shallow but the double headed shower was lovely although not particularly powerful. Some guests must walk into their rooms looking for things to complain about, but I cannot honestly think of anything worth complaining about. We loved this hotel, it was spacious, comfortable and clean and ideally located for the theatres. We highly recommend it and would definately stay here again.

<Author>Indecisive_traveller
<Content>Oasis in the middle of all the action! My sister and I stayed at the Westin New York at Times Square over Easter weekend this year (April 6-10, 2007). We were really happy with our decision to stay at this hotel for several reasons: First of all, some details about the hotel: We liked the contemporary decor and the fact that it was very well-maintained. Having read some of the reviews of other NY hotels, we were prepared for small rooms - however, this was not the case! The room was also very nicely decorated and well laid out - the bathroom was very clean and everything was in good working order - I loved the shower!! Bed linens are a big thing for me - I've noticed that with age, my imagination gets a bit overactive with all the ways in which dirty linens can come about. But these were always kept extremely clean - and the beds, pillows and comforter were extremely comfortable - I actually found myself looking forward to going to bed! I also found the rooms exceedingly quiet. No street noise whatsoever.The staff at the hotel were also extremely helpful. On our last day, my sister and I had done some last minute shopping and were frantically trying to repack our suitcases. They were extremely accomodating as we turned part of the lobby into a packing room - apparently, they said this was a common occurrence! Also, I had had an item delivered to the hotel while we were out, and when we returned, it was not with the front desk as I had originally been told. Still, no worries at all, as a staff member thoroughly investigated the matter and got to the bottom of it, while I continued to pack! This was my first time to NY, so I have to admit that I was a bit apprehensive about the location - was it going to be safe? I quickly discovered that I had nothing to worry about! Although the hotel was located in a very busy area, I never once felt unsafe going out about during the daytime or at nigh). There is a strong police presence (the police headquarters is located just a couple of blocks a way), but I loved that everything (ie restaurants, subway, stores, bus station) was within steps of this hotel. I also found that many of the larger chains (eg HMV, Sephora) were open quite late into the night (10pm or later). And I was also pleasantly surprised to find the salespeople extremely friendly and helpful! My only piece of advice - be prepared for the crowds! I have never been to a city where the sidewalks are almost always packed with pedestrians - many of which are tourists, I imagine. The subway is literally just around the corner from the hotel, so getting to farther destinations was no problem. As you can imagine, shopping was a key priority for us - we made our way to Century 21, the Soho district (where by the way, many stores were open on Easter Sunday!!), Filene's Basement with no problem. We also could have taken the subway easily to 5th Avenue - but we decided to take about a 20-minute walk up to Central Park, and then walk down 5th Avenue, which is a must, if only to window shop! We also went to Woodbury Commons, a humongous outdoor outlet mall in New Jersey. Bus tours depart from Port Authority, which is just kitty corner to the Westin.While our main focus was on shoppng, if you can only spend a short time in this city, and want to see the 'key' tourist sites, then this hotel is an ideal choice because it is in a central location. I absolutely fell in love with the city, and I'd like to come back and visit New York again at a more leisurely pace with my husband (but we'll probably choose to stay in an area that's a little less hectic than Times Square).

<Author>daisy47
<Content>Beautiful hotel, wonderful location Stayed at the Westin Times Square May 27, 2007 for one night and it was very nice. It was a surprise trip from my husband so I do not know how much it cost for the night.We pulled up and used the valet parking. It was $48 for 24 hours. You have the option to park yourself for a little cheaper or they will park it for the $48. We chose to valet but if you are trying to save money, there is a garage across the street where you can park for 24 hours and I believe it was $36. The location of the hotel is wonderful for tourists. It is one block from Times Square (no views of Times Square). It is located in the Theater District. There are tons of restaurants, movie theaters, live theaters, and stores on the same block. The lobby was very nice. A large modern lobby with lots of seating, a concierge and a large front desk with no one waiting so we walked right up.When we went to check in, the man at the front desk who helped us was very nice. We asked for a room with a great view and he went in back to check what rooms were available. We got a room on the 43rd floor with the perfect view of the Empire State Building and the Hudson River and basically all of Lower Manhattan. The room was very nice. There was a flat screen TV, a desk, chair, a big bed, two phones, and a safe and mini bar in the closet. The bed was very comfortable (a Heavenly bed) although I enjoy the Sheraton Sweet Sleeper bed better. There were foam and feather pillows. The bathroom was very pretty. It was all black slate and there was a nice sized tub (not a Jacuzzi). The sink was a weird stainless steel and kind of reminded us of a prison sink. :) There was one bathrobe to use.The room was quiet for a NYC room. You could scarcely hear horns honking and fire trucks but it was fine. The curtains and shade blocked out most of the light but there was one side that didn't close all of the way so there was a bit of streaming light in the morning.You can open your window a crack and hear the sounds of the city.Shula's restaurant is inside the hotel. We looked at the breakfast menu but it was very expensive for basic food (like room service) and there are so many breakfast places nearby that we didn't stay.We called the concierge and they were very quick and helpful with all of the information we needed.The day of check out we left our bags with the bellhops downstairs. They asked when we would be back and gave us a claim card and we were on our way.When we came back, it took no time to get our bags and the valet took about 15 minutes to bring us our car. We were told it would take 20-30 minutes to get the car back. If you leave your car longer than the 24 hours, they will charge you another $48 so pick it up on time. The valets were somewhat rude. They were taking care of many people at a time. It took some time to get their attention and they were talking to each other. Then one took my claim check, called it in and walked away to help with a taxi who he was yelling at. Then when the car arrived (with the radio and bass blasting on a radio that had 1. been turned off when we left it and 2. the channel had been changed), another valet asked for the claim check and we had to find the other valet who had taken it and he confirmed that he had it (although he never looked so I guess he memorized it). They seemed slightly disorganized and unprofessional. Overall, the hotel was wonderful, the room was comfortable and it is in a perfect location.

<Author>Larchmoor
<Content>Haven in a hectic place The Westin is located in a block between 42nd and 43rd St on 8th Avenue, about 2 minute walk from Times Square and close to many theatres. The area is pretty lively day and night. I had no sense of any safety concerns. Plenty of people and cops around. The Port Authority Bus Terminal (and subways) are very near, which is handy for subway trips. Reception is up an escalator on the first floor (2nd floor US), wherea sitting area and the usual front desk services are available. Theredid not appear to be and food or drink service available to those seated on chairs or sofas in the reception area.We had booked a King Executive Club, and used the Starwood Best Rate Guarantee to secure the same rate that Expedia was offering ($393, inc taxes), which was a good rate for NYC. I am a Starwood Platinum member, but an upgrade was unavailable at check-in, although we got one a few days later. The Executive Club allows access to a Club on the 8th floor which serves continental breakfast and evening hors d'oeuvres. This is a pleasant extra, although at times the Club was pretty packed for breakfast and the selection of food items suffered accordingly. The Room on the 15th floor was not huge, but pleasantly laid out and clean. It was modernly decorated with a plasma TV and an iMac computer (I am a Mac fan). The view was not great from the window.From the lobby, it was possible to leave the hotel and exit on 43rd St or go through the lobby of a cinema/movie theatre and exit on 42nd St. We mostly used the 42nd St exit. Halfway through our stay we were upgraded to a Junior Suite. on the 30th Floor. This had a much better view over the west side of the city to the Hudson, and although not huge, had a nice sitting area. The rooms are served by 2 blocks of elevators, one serving 2nd floor (reception area) to 23rd, and the other running from the 2nd direct to 23 through 45th. That means if you want to go from a floor above 23 to the Club (on 8), you have to switch elevators. Not ideal, but not a huge deal either. Internet access was available in each room for $14.95 a day. This was pretty fast - no complaints. We did not use the Spa. I had breakfast one morning in Shula's - a la carte selection of hot breakfast including Eggs Benedict, bacon, sausage etc etc. Overall, I would say this hotel is pretty much what you would expect of a Westin. If I were going back to NYC, I would have no problems staying there again.

<Author>Tilly99
<Content>Will be forever indebted to housekeeping and security While we were quite pleased with our weekend room at the Westin NY Times Square, it was the excellent personal attention of the housekeeping staff and a security guard who made our stay beautifully memorable. I am long overdue in writing this review. Last Spring, our family stayed at the Westin, where my husband had a weekend conference. In the Sunday morning packing frenzy, our son's favorite stuffed toy, a beloved yellow dog named Puggy, was left behind. At home later that night, our son rummaged through his suitcase, panicked: Puggy was gone. I called the hotel, explained our dilemma, and was transferred to security. A man-- who I'm sure had more important things to do-- took a few minutes to sort through the Lost and Found box. I waited with bated breath. A little yellow dog? he asked. I've got it right here! Puggy was sent the next morning, and arrived on Tuesday in a Fed Ex box, courtesy of the Westin at Times Square. Our son was delighted, and so were we. In what has to be one of the busiest hotels in the world, a few caring people took the time to make all the difference for one small boy and his family. For this, we will always be grateful. Even Puggy is looking forward to our next visit.

<Author>krimar
<Content>The Good, The Bad, and The Ugly The location of this hotel can not be beat if you would like to stay within walking distance of Times Square and the theater district. Request a room on a high floor with a view and you will not be disappointed. The good: the customer service at this hotel is exemplary. The employees are helpful and aim to please. If you have any problems with your stay and talk to the employees about the problem in a calm manner, they will be very happy to please you. We stayed here during the Easter holiday weekend, and the bad is things were not perfect. We arrived well ahead of check-in time, and as the hotel was sold out the night prior to our arrival, rooms were not ready. We completed our early check in, dropped our bags with the bell-hop, and proceeded to site see in the city. Mistake #1: we assumed that a call back to check on the status of our rooms was not necessary, although they will give you a card with information to do so. I suggest you do make the call. When we arrived back to the hotel at 4:00PM (an hour after the official check-in time and six hours after we completed the early check-in process), one of the rooms in our party was not ready. They sent the family we were traveling with to the room after the computer showed it was clean. When the family arrived, it was not clean. The hotel quickly relocated the family to a suite. This particular suite was in a different part of the building. While the room had no view, it did have a very nice computer and access to a free continental breakfast and happy hour in a separate lounge area. The bathroom was larger, but the rest of the room did not seem any bigger than the room we had. The hotel also deducted 100.00 from the price of the room for the trouble the family went through with the room not being ready by check-in time. We had three problems of our own: they misplaced a bag, which they quickly found; the outlets stopped working after my daughter and I both used hairdryers at the same time (which was fixed within ten minutes); and the water was tepid on the day we checked out (they explained there was some problem they were working on that affected some rooms that day.) When I checked out and was asked, How was your stay? I informed the clerk of the three problems we encountered. The clerk for our room also made a nice deduction from our tab for the inconveninces we experienced. Both rooms were also provided coupons for numerous free drinks at one of the hotels two restaurants (including Shula's.)  The hotel itself reminded me of the Delano in Miami--two story high curtains; large white candles in glass containers the shapes of congos; a very modern feel to it--very nice in taste and decor. And again, the location was fantastic. Times Square and the theaters, are all within walking distance, as is Rockefeller Center for those whose stamina will allow them a fifteen to twenty minute walk. The subway, of course, is nearby as well. No ugly really exists for this hotel. The staff is extremely accomdating, so if you experience any problems, they will quickly remedy them. The location can't be beat. I am confident if you have a problem and calmly explain it to a front desk employee, they will do everything in their power to help you.

Kind of random, of all the things to do away with why the clock? The heavenly bed was nice but the towels and bathrobe were somewhat frayed. The special heavenly towel was frayed and the belt loop on the bathrobe was coming off. If I'm staying in a hotel room with two beds shouldn't there be two bathrobes in the room? Just an idea... The bathroom was quite dusty; when I dried my hair lots of dust was flying around the room. Also a few random purple marker stains were on the bedspread. Not a deal breaker, but it's the little things that I notice.No turn down service that I'm aware of. Again, it's the little touches that I expect to see when I pay that much money.All in all the hotel is nice, but I guess I just expected something a bit more personal.

<Author>RdTripMom
<Content>OK But Not Spectacular The Westin is a decent hotel, clean and well-situated. But it is not a dazzling hotel and for the price, I expected more. The rooms are on the small side although the views are nice and the beds are comfy. There isn't a taxi stand so you need to get one on the street if the doorman is busy. When we return to NYC, though, we'll go back to the Hyatt at Grand Central -- it has more zip.

The breakfast wasn't as good as in other hotels but it was adequate and was enough to set you up for the day. You have 2 kinds of fresh juice, tea/coffee, oatmeal, cereals, fruits (including 3 kinds of melon), cold meats, cheese, pastries, muffins and toast. The lounge has good views so you can watch the world also. Only downside was that it was never very warm unless you were sitting away from the windows and then you didn't have the view! Overall the staff in the hotel were very helpful and we had a nice spacious room for all of our shopping bags. The so-called heavenly bed is also great. Very comfortable.When we are lucky enough to go back to NY we will definitely book back into this hotel.
