<Author>Hawaii_Girl
<Content>INSIDER TIP: "Don't pay extra for the Club Lounge!" We're SPG Platinum so the club lounge is free, but for anyone paying the extra money for a Club Room is going to be sorely disappointed! Here's what made us laugh:The lounge charges $5 for wine or beer, which is only available from 6-8pm. The cabernet was a thumbs down, but an inexpensive lesson considering it's $21 for the small bottle of cabernet from the mini-bar. Be careful: they use the automatic sensor system so if you pick it up, you get charged! I'm sure the hotel removes charges for items that weren't actually consumed, so be sure to review your bill before paying.Another first during breakfast - boiled eggs in ice water! We've been to several countries and hundreds of hotels in the US but this made me say, Huh?!? I don't get it..... - the eggs are peeled, which is a nice gesture, but why ice water? Why not warm water? Lastly, my dad complained there wasn't any fruit but, alas there was! I jokingly pointed to the baskets of green apples. I guess we've just been spoiled by the Westin Shanghai or the Sheraton Frankfurt where there's a variety of freshly cut fruit, free drinks all day, a large spread of hot and cold foods (not Nutri-Grain bars or bags of potato chips) and bacon, potatoes and made-to-order eggs in the morning.This is a wonderful hotel, but I would hate to see anyone waste their money on a Club Room (which by the way are on the 8th floor, low enough to hear the sirens and honking, so if you're a light sleeper, then this is definitely not for you!). PS - broadband internet in the room is $14.95 + tax for 24 hours. The hotel says the wireless internet access is no longer free in the lobby but I've noticed you can still get online, though it's a little iffy.... for example it would work on a certain page, but when I would click on a link, it would reroute to the Westin login page. A little frustrating, but if you just need to check emails, you might want to try the lobby first before accepting the daily rate charge.

<Author>SophieJinx
<Content>Our Favorite Place in the Big Expensive City! We live about two hours outside New York and every once in a while an early business meeting will inspire us to stay overnight. We've tried some other places (like the W Lexington Avenue) but have really come to consider the Westin our home hotel.Whether NY small (like London small!) or splurge-worthy corners (our last room, fabulous) the rooms are well appointed, sleek and contemporary without being...over the top...and cozy. The bedding is superb. Our last trip -- last week -- my husband booked a corner room on a high floor (it was about $475, a bit of a splurge) but we loved it! The room had a foyer, and then wrap around windows; the main part of the room was outfitted with flat screen, desk, benches, nice bathroom....One caveat: we've eaten at the hotel's restaurant -- Don Shula's -- a few times. It's a typical steakhouse (where your sides are separate) and the food is excellent but the prices are a bit breathtaking, particularly for wine. We couldn't find a bottle under $44 (and that one was out of stock) -- and few were under $70. I realize it's NY and it's an expense account restaurant but still....Service was also totally chaotic (and it wasn't even busy yet) though we did appreciate the gesture, by the maitre'd (she was a woman, not sure what you call her); she'd overheard us say we were celebrating our anniversary and arranged for us to be surprised with a lovely chocolate dessert. What a nice touch! Made up for the early roughness of service.The bar at the Westin is fun -- quite a scene -- and you can order snack food there. We might try that next time. And of course, a whole range of restaurants are nearby. The lobby has free wireless (it's kinda' pricey in the rooms).We asked for a late checkout and the hotel was quite accommodating. All in all -- excellent experience.

<Author>JohnJB
<Content>Don't believe the publicity... If you read about this hotel on the Starwood website or any others for that matter, you will see their PR makes a great deal about the stunning architecture, interior and terrific location of this hotel.Firstly you would need to be a contortionist to appreciate the architecture of this hotel as it is shoehorned into a tacky side street a block away from Times Square from which the only sign that a hotel is on the site is the apologetic entrance at street level. From that entrance (20 yards from which you will se the delights of drunks sleeping on the sidewalk) you need to take an escalator to the lobby which is rather grey and unwelcoming. The rooms are fairly small but clean and bathrooms adequate. Views from the 40th floor are trumpeted as stunning but, as high as we were, I was unable to see anything of interest save for rooftops of adjacent hotels/office blocks.Also - don't get carried away by the concept of having a 'club room'. The 'club' facilities were housed in a smallish room on the 8th floor where an inadequate breakfast and sparse evening canapes are served. Waste of money!As regards location, Times Square is local to most NY tourist attractions but don't spoil your vacation by staying there - it is very very unpleasant during the daytime and slightly threatening after dark. There are hundreds of hotels in NY that don't suffer the disadvantages of the Westin - book one of those instead.

<Author>wwtravelr
<Content>Sad if this is the best Starwood can do in NYC I am a 25 year veteran of Starwood's best hotels around the world - in the US, Asia and Europe - we are big fans, and I am sadly disappointed with this effort in NYC.We stayed in the Westin Times Square in early December 2006 with moderate expectations based on reviews from this site. And to be fair, nothing was terribly wrong - it's just that nothing was terribly right either. Overall I would say that the service and physical plant of the hotel was highly disappointing.Let me start with the sole positive from our stay: We had luggage wrapped in plastic from our return flight from South Africa. A very courteous gentleman from the maintenance staff saw us coming down the hall and offered to cut open the plastic. When we offered him a tip, he graciously refused, saying it was his pleasure to help us.Starting with check in: we were greeted by a young man at the Preferred Checkin counter who couldn't muster a smile or eye contact. His manner was somewhere between indifferent and curt. We truly felt we were imposing on him when asking if we might check in. And at the time of our check in the lobby was empty - no lines, not busy, no excuse for this kind of attitude. This sort of set the tone for the whole stay.We were in a Club Room, which I would not recommend in this case (although we almost always prefer club floors at Westins around the world). Although the room came equipped with a nice new Mac computer, we would frankly rather have had that investment go into updating the tired carpet and walls or part of the dingy bathroom. Or include (as almost every other premium hotel does on their version of club floors) free access to the internet. I will say the bed was fine - clean sheets, firm, etc. But the industry is at a point now where this alone doesn't get you a whole lot of extra credit points.The Club Lounge itself was tired, and the staff there seemed even more tired than the room, and almost studiedly unhelpful when we asked questions or for assistance. We got the distinct feeling that if we dropped dead in front of them they wouldn't stop reading their magazines, as this would be 'not my job'. They were clearly not the cream of the crop which, again, you sort of expect in Club Lounges.A list of further small gripes, just in case someone from Starwood/Westin reads these reviews:The coffee table in our club room was terrible - peeling black paint on a cheap table which looked at least a dozen years old.The bathroom sink was a dented tin-can effect. Not chic-art, just old, cheap and dented.Throughout our stay the 'Service Express' line couldn't answer a single question for us, and really didn't seem interested in finding anyone who could. After disconnecting me three times when transferring to the Concierge, I had to forcefully insist that the Service Express operator stay on the line until he had connected me with a real person who could answer my question.The walls in the hotel are thin. Really thin. Several times we could clearly overhear conversations from our neighbor, and they seemed to be talking at a normal (not loud) volume.Local phone calls are charged at $2.50. Okay, so some places still do this, but with the falling cost of calls and when you are in a Club Room you don't expect this kind of highway robbery.There were no slippers, not even the inexpensive $0.50 ones you find in mid-range hotels. And our query to find out if we could get some was given a rude response from the Service Express operator.

<Author>KTC-NewEngland(CT)
<Content>Good, but not amazing. We chose the Westin Times Square specifically based on the good reviews here at Trip Advisor. We stayed for 2 nights in a Club level room (1424) which was a larger corner room. It does not have amazing views being relatively low on the 14th floor. As for city noises, it was quiet enough. We heard sirens every now and then but not regular traffic noise. The Club lounge (on 8th floor) is not extraordinary.......it offers a continental breakfast (only warm item was oatmeal) and then an evening hors d'oeuvres offering, which was much better. Free teas, coffees and soft drinks are available all day long. The location of the hotel is excellent........it really is in the thick of it, and maybe even too much for our tastes. Times Square was crazy crowded even just to cross through to get to other midtown locations. There are lots of dining choices, movie theatres and subway stations just out the hotel doors. We normally would stay at the Rihga but it is now The London and not family friendly any longer. We had 2 kids and this room had plenty of roll-around floor space for them. Each window had a window seat for looking out and they liked that. There is also one club chair and one desk chair. We ordered dinner room service and used the beds for seating purposes.Hotel parking = $45 per day......the steepest we have ever paid in NYC.My only real complaint is that the bathroom door is glass and anytime someone turned on the light during the night or early morning, the room was lit up as a result. I called for a night light but there were none. A night light would easily fix the problem. The double roller blinds do an excellent job of making the room dark.Enjoy your stay.

This hotel is in a perfect location. A block from Times Square. A short walk and you are in the middle of everything. <Author>lylach
<Content>Great room, great service My husband and I recently stayed at the Westin Times Square for three nights as part of our first wedding anniversary vacation. We spent our last three nights at a different hotel in a different neighborhood so we could explore more on foot - the change of hotels was planned ahead of time, not as a result of poor service.I have to admit that I was pleasantly surprised with the level of service that we experienced during our stay at the Westin. Our check-in process went smoothly and our room was ready for us upon arrival, which was around 4:00 p.m. We were given a corner room on the 38th floor and had great views of Times Square as well as the Empire State Building and the Husdon River, since we had windows on two sides of the room. The New York Times is building a new skyscraper 2 blocks down the street, and our room overlooked the building's skeleton.As always, the Westin Heavenly Bed truly is heaven to sleep in. Our tired legs and feet didn't want to get out of bed in the morning! The bathroom was really small, however. There was practically no counter space and the two of us had to take turns getting ready, which always seemed to put us behind schedule. The two shower heads in the shower were nice though and felt good on our tired bodies at the end of a long day exploring the city. When we got up to the room, we realized that we wanted to have a separate refrigerator sent up (the mini bar charges you if you move anything in it) to store some food and drink in during our stay. We also needed a corkscrew to open a bottle of wine. They were very prompt and both items were delivered within about 10-15 minutes. I was expecting not to see them until we came back from dinner. The daily maid service was always very good and our room was cleaned to our satisfaction every day. We tipped $2 per night and that seemed to be sufficient for the maid to give us good service. Some people mentioned a noise problem, which is an issue that I am very sensitive to, but we didn't have any problems. We could hear fire engines and ambulances on the street, but that was it. We couldn't hear the people in the rooms next to us, or above us. The temperature control of the room was very easy and we were able to change it with no problems. I loved that you could choose from 3 different fan speeds, so the high speed at night was great white noise, which I'm used to having at home. Elevators were always very fast and efficient, didn't take long to get up and down from the 38th floor. Security seems good, as we had to show our room keys when walking in at street level at night before being able to go up the escalators to the lobby and elevators. That's a welcome feature given the sheer volume of people that are always around the Times Square area. We didn't eat at any of the hotel restaurants, so can't review their quality. We did try to get internet access at the business center and had some troubles. The computer kept freezing up on me and we quickly ran out of our paid 15 minutes of access. We immediately told the business center attendant about the problem and she called the internet access comapny and got our card credited for the $6.95 we had paid for 15 minutes of internet access. Problem resolved with no problems or questions asked. I was pleasantly surprised once again! Overall, I'd definitely recommend the Westin Times Square, especially for first time visitors to NYC. The hotel itself did a great job. If the hotel were in a different location, I'd stay there again, but the craziness and high volume of people always in the Times Square area was overwhelming to us.

Our Bellman AL was very personable and helpful. Elevators were working at all times. Mexican restaurant, steakhouse, starbucks and movie theater all accessible from inside the hotel. At night upon returning to the hotel we were asked to show our room key this made us feel safe. Pajama Game, Hard Rock Cafe just steps away. You have to visit Bryant Park it was so NY!!!!!! I am already planning to return to the city. I can't believe that I have lived so close to the city all my life and never planned a trip here before. Book your trip today and have a great time, we did!!!!!!

<Content>May 6th - Location, Location, Location If you want to stay in the heart of everything - this is the place. Went to NYC last weekend. The beds were clean, and heavenly. Let's face it - you are not in the room enough for little things to really matter. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not good Like most of the other people who recently stayed at the Westin, I was also really disappointed. It really seems to be the housekeeping that is letting down this property, as we experienced many of the same problems as the others: sheets were not changed, there were no hand towels, used up toiletries were not replaced, and our do not disturb sign was missing, which meant that the maid disturbed us every morning. Even when we pointed out that the sign was missing , they didnt bring us another one. For two consecutive days we didnt have any hand towels. Our room was not cleaned very well. We also asked for extra hangers and didnt get any. This hotel has a great look and design, but its also very cold and impersonal, and when the only contact you have is with the housekeeping, and thats not a good experience, it leaves a bad impression. Also, Westin has been running a lot of magazine ads, promoting the white tea scent of the new Westin. Well I never experienced any of this scent in my room, or in the lobby or any part of the hotel, so I don't know what that's all about. When I asked at the front desk, they didn't have a clue what I was talking about - apparently a major breakdown in communication between the marketing department and the actual hotels. I thought, well, I'm going to walk into this hotel, and it's going to smell great, and be relaxing etc - but the only thing I could smell was the ketchup and mustard on the hot dogs that people were walking in with from outside. I'd also read in the descriptions about this amazing beam of light splitting the building in two - never saw it. I wouldn't stay here again - it has the potential of being an amazing hotel, but you can't rely on fancy design and architecture alone, its the quality of your staff and the service you give your guests that really makes or breaks the day. I expected much more.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Excellent hotel The Westin Hotel Times Square is a wonderful place to stay in New York City. It is a quiet, modern hotel. We have stayed there twice and wouldn't stay anywhere else. It is located within a block of the Port Authority Bus Terminal where you can catch the Newark, New Jersey bus to the airport. We highly recommend the red Grayline Sightseeing bus (on and off privileges) as you can see all burrows and sites. We also recommend the Circleline boat tour around Manhattan Island. You can purchase both of these tours on a combined ticket at the Port Authority or at the Grayline ticket office a couple blocks from the hotel. This hotel is located in the theater district and within walking distance of many shows. We saw The Producers and Lion King...both were excellent. We did not care for the hotel restaurant, but great restaurants of all prices are located very close to the hotel. We especially enjoyed John's Pizza, Bubba Gump's and Rosey O'Grady's....inexpensive restaurants and very good. Both restaurants are within walking distance of the hotel. We visited in 2004 and 2005.

<Author>musicmom3
<Content>Convenient location We enjoyed our recent stay at the Westin. We took advantage of a spring discount for the room and then added an upgrade to the club floor, which allowed us a complimentary continental breakfast and evening snacks and non-alcoholic beverages (wine and beer are on the honor system, where you fill out a voucher for a $5 charge per glass). It was great to not have to pile on the winter coats and fight the wind first thing in the morning, and the evening snack (pasta in vodka sauce with substantial bread sticks and a variety of vegetable salads) actually turned out to be dinner for myself and daughters. We had asked for an early checkin (9:00 AM) and our room was ready, which was a great start to our day in NYC. The location of the hotel is great, close to everything. The heavenly beds were heavenly, but I didn't see much heavenly about the bathroom, but then we had a wheelchair accessible bathroom with a hand-held shower spray instead of the double showerhead. The people at the Westin were all extremely friendly and helpful, and the service was excellent. My one warning would be for light sleepers. We were on the 16th floor facing the Port Authority Station, and there were horns blaring all night. Light sleepers might want to have another room location.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Go for a High Floor We stayed at the Westin Times Square for 10 days in january. The quality of stay at this hotel is very much dependent on the floor you are on. We know, because after four nights of street noise hell, we moved rooms and enjoyed ourselves thoroughly. Here is the problem, and it is really a problem if you are noise sensitive. The hotel itself is located at 43rd and 8th Avenue, not exactly my favorite location but incredibly accessible to public transportation. Unfortunately, this location is one of the busiest and loudest in the city. The hotel employs two different window systems. The system on the lower levels leaks noise like a sieve. So for four nights we could barely sleep. Traffic, sirens, you name it, could be heard in the room. The room itself was fine. After complaining, we were given a room much higher in the hotel. Lo and behold, the window system was entirely different, and it kept out virtually all noise. We then became happy campers.The public areas were reasonable for a business hotel and the friendliness of the staff depended on whom you were dealing with. We originally stayed on the club level, so we had gym and breakfast as part of the room cost. The gym was small but nice. The buffet breakfast was iffy at best - ok if you weren't looking for a real meal. For some unexplainable reason, there was no consistency from day to day as to what was being served. Once we got by the noise issue, our stay was excellent. We would definitely stay at the hotel again, provided we had a room with the better window system. Otherwise, we would pass.

<Author>martdm
<Content>Nice hotel; spa room not all it's cracked up to be In town for a concert at the Nokia theater around the corner, we recently stayed the weekend in one of this hotel's spa inspired rooms. In general this is a nice hotel, typical of Westin standards. The location is very good if you wish to be near Times Square and the surrounding areas, as well as to major subway lines.We didn't find the spa room to necessarily be worth the price of the upgrade. The massage chair (our main impetus for reserving the room) was not terribly comfortable, providing no benefit to the legs or feet while being a bit too harsh on the back (even on the lowest settings). The spa bath products were nice but only provided in the typical small hotel packaging, which was not really enough to thoroughly enjoy.The 23rd floor corner room itself was very nice with windows surrounding the outside walls and a view of the river. The bathroom was large by NYC standards and had a spacious tub/shower we loved. The 'heavenly bed' left my husband and I disappointed as we really did not sleep well on it (perhaps it's an acquired comfort as we're used to a more firm mattress as opposed to the memory foam type overlay the mattress has). The pillows were divine and the bed clothes were very nice.Everything was very clean and well kept throughout our stay. The street noise however was a bit loud in the morning.The few staff we encountered throughout our stay were friendly and helpful and we had no problem arranging airport transportation through the concierge or late checkout through the customer service staff. All in all, this was a good stay and perhaps we would return if we needed a hotel in this particular vicinity once again.

There were long hairs on the desk chair and dust on the furniture.We went back to the front desk and asked for a change of room which was greeted without a problem and the next day the change took place, albeit that there was confusion between the front desk and bellman as to whether the room was available or not, buy hey, this is a big hotel and it was busy. No problem.Our next room on 40th floor was much better, away from the lifts and had an even better view of the first, looking across Manhattan with a view of the soaring Empire State even when lying in bed! However, be warned that this is not a quiet hotel. There may be heavenly beds but the noise of people and doors clanging in the corridors simply couldn't be avoided and this was through until our departure on 6 Jan when the New Year crowd had all gone. Also, housekeeping arrive on the corridors about 8.30am and talk loudly. This simply wasn't on. Then there's the decor. The rooms look a bit like they've been furnished out of Ikea. Okay for while I guess but I'm not sure I would want to check into this hotel in say, 5 years. The rooms will be falling apart. The brushed steel sinks and units reminded me of a cross between prison cell ones (not that I've been arrested!!) and operating theatres, and our heavenly bath had yellow staining by the taps, so we used the heavenly shower which was like, er, a regular shower. However, yes, the heavenly beds are just that, heavenly, but like I said earlier, shame about the noise outside the room that woke us.Having said all this, the views were great, Bar 10 and Shula's were excellent. The staff in these establishments far exceeded that of the hotel staff which is very unsusual I think.What grated on us at the end of our stay was that housekeeping just gave up on the last day and didn't bother attending on us. We made a request at 2pm and another at 7pm and 8pm and then at 9pm someone finally brought some towels. This made us late for plans for out last night in NY and the attitude of staff was appalling. The front desk made no apology said it was sold out so housekeeping was on a request basis. 1) I did request it, 2) how would I know that the place was sold out anyway, and 3) I have never heard of this system in this standard of hotel before.When we finally got out that night, someone came and made the bed and took the rubbish but that was it. No refill of soap, water, coffee, tidy up etc.Then, on the day of check out, a $250 charge had mysteriously appeared on our bill from the health club. Not thinking this would be a problem if I raised it, I was greeted with suspicion and unprofessionalism. A call was made in front of me to the health club and I was made to wait. I was then told that I had signed a check and that it was being faxed over. When it arrived it clearly was not my signature but had my name on it. It also had a different room number. After a further wait and sample of my signature, I was told that the amount would be cleared and that they would investigate further. I understand that this may not have been the hotel's fault, or it may have simply been an error but what I did not like was the way I was made to feel as though I was pulling a fast one, and how there was no apology for the mistake and for taking up my time. During my waiting at the desk, I also discovered that I had been charged an extra $50 per night on my rate. In essence, the majority of front desk staff could use a training course on hospitality and customer relations. We then left, rather annoyed, tainting our stay at the Westin but certainly not New York! In future we'll stay elsewhere, and for $429 and $329 a night respectively, it will be in a far superior hotel if we avoid the holiday season.

<Author>Use2trvl
<Content>First Class all the way Stayed at the Westin-Times Square Christmas week. In spite of the crowds, we were treated exceptionally at the hotel. When we checked in, we requested a room high up. We were put on the 22nd floor and had a great view of the Empire State Building. A real thrill for our kids since we were not going to wait 2 hours to go to the top of the Empire State Building.The concierge was great. The rooms were quite large and there were four of us in there. Two months prior, I shared a room at the Paramount Hotel in NYC. That room was about 1/2 the size of the Westin and costs significantly more.Great location. Can't be beat if you are a tourist looking to experience all that NYC has to offer.Regarding the heavenly shower. The person that wrote the review about not having the second showerhead work did not miss out on much. It took us quite a while to figure out how to work it. When we did, it was no great shakes. The head of the shower was not like a shower massage so you couldn't place pulsating water on your back while experiencing rain water on your head. It did look cool, but that's about it.Room Service in NYC??? Who needs it when you can have any kind of food delivered to the lobby. The concierge can certainly recommend good places that deliver.Also, for those interested in going to the theatre...The concierge does not arrange theatre tickets. There is a private operation that runs the ticket concession in the hotel and you'll pay quite a premium to secure your tickets. We just walked to the box office (2 blocks away) and even during Christmas week, secured tickets to a popular show. You just have to be flexible (i.e., have three nights in mind) and you will do fine. Of course if you have money to burn and you don't mind paying extra, use the service.

<Author>jad376
<Content>After my third stay, I've moved on. Just like in showbiz, this sleek, modern star's fifteen minutes are almost up. The beds are amazing, and will still cause you to sleep through your alarm clock even after the lights have dimmed and the curtain has gone down. However, that premiere-night glow faded from my mind during my third stay here last spring. It wasn't because this is a bad hotel - the location is ideal for tourists and theatregoers, there's a movie theater  starbucks off the lobby, the security is tight, the food from Shula's is good and the rooms are luxurious (in the kind of way a Mondrian painting is deep)...but...I began to sense a kind of sterility to this place that speaks of modern, 21st century New New York. Not that there's anything bad about stainless steel  granite bathrooms, rice paper auto-brightening flourescent lamps, Herman Miller 'Aeron' desk chairs  massive glass windows. I guess I just prefer the feeling of creature comforts to a style that forces itself to be newer than everything around it without breathing in the aroma of the old. I predict this hotel will become dated within this decade, which is sometimes a problem when you hire famous young architects to do an important urban development. The designers had the foresight - and the license - to build a hotel that ignores its fleeting neighborhood context and instead embraces being an iconic part of the Theater District. As such, as a tourist, you will most likely either be entertained or nonplussed by this. Ultimately, the real hotel stuff - the beds, the shower, the service - will win you over, but the hit-or-miss attitude of the staff, for the moment, takes one star away from my rating. My defense of the staff is that this is an enormous hotel that, when compared to other comparably sized upscale tourist hotels in Midtown (Hilton 54th st, Sheraton 53rd st, Marriott Marquis), makes an effort to be a cut above. So, fellow travelers, regardless of what I think of the atmosphere and the creature comforts, the Westin is a great pick when you can get a good rate and, oh, follow these tips:-Make sure you request a corner room (4039 has two queen beds and an AMAZING view of northeast Manhattan all the way around to the empire state building - I could see Rockefeller Center and a bite of Central Park from the toilet. 1929, with a king bed, is on the bottom of the tower part, but I could still see down into much of 42nd. st, and across Chelsea with a sweeping view of the Hudson river.). -Trust the good reviews of Shula's steaks -If you can't get a parking package deal, Self-park your car for around $16/day in the secure garages on 62nd. st  west end ave. (+ $5 cab ride to hotel, or walk + $2 subway ride) instead of valet for over $45 (they lost my bloody car once and made me over an hour late) -There's a bakery-cafe in the building, accessible from the street only, around the corner from the front entrance on 43rd  8th avenue. We did take-out breakfast from here every morning after being charged over $60 for eggs, fruit, croissants and coffee from room service.-The New York Times headquarters will be under construction directly across 42nd st. for the next couple of years. All the rooms in the lower (orange + yellow) part of the hotel, the atrium section which is depicted in the traveler from the UK's photographs, will probably be subjected to a great deal of additional noise. I think these rooms are club floor rooms, but I'd stay away from this part of the building during construction. Be forewarned and request something higher up, or overlooking 43rd street. -Take my review and recommendations with a grain of salt, please. Happy traveling!

<Author>siouxzy
<Content>Outstanding Stay in a Convenient Location! We stayed at the Westin Times Square November 22-24 while in NYC to see the 2005 Macy's Thanksgiving Day Parade; I found a great deal on an Executive Club Level room through Expedia. The location was outstanding! I've stayed at many hotels in NYC  this was probably the best stay I've had. The hotel is located right in the heart of Times Square, 2 subway stops are less then half a block away which is very convenient. The staff that we encountered were all very professional  pleasant (no one hinted at being tipped as mentioned in some of the other reviews. However I recently noticed that an unauthorized $10 tip was charged to my credit card which I plan to look into.) Since it was Thanksgiving week, at check-in we were given a packet of information about the Macy's parade, other events in the area  some of the big stores' holiday hours which was nice. The hotel elevators were very fast, we never had to wait for one. Our room was very spacious, comfortable  clean, with modern decor  a live plant on the desk, a Bose radio/CD player on the night stand  a bathrobe; 2 bottles of imported water, Starbucks in-room coffee  a morning newspaper were provided complementary each day. One nice room feature was the windows in our room could be opened a bit if you'd like some outside air or want to bask in the sounds of NYC for a moment without leaving your room. The Heavenly bed was just that, VERY heavenly! The Heavenly shower was also nice with extra room, dual shower heads  deluxe cotton towels. The evening turn down service was a nice touch complete with chocolates on the pillow  a little card stating the next day's weather forecast. The complimentary breakfast was fine, it consisted of the usual coffee, juice, bagels, Danish  cereal. We didn't get a chance to take advantage for the complimentary hors d'oeuvres in the evening because we were out  about. There is an AMC theatre, Starbucks  a few restaurants connected to the hotel, you can reach them all without stepping outside which was convenient. The Westin tends to be quite pricey for obvious reasons but if you can get a good deal (esp on the Club Level) go for it! I would stay here again  recommend it to others. For a casual lunch or dinner try Viva Pancho @ W. 44th, a good, moderately priced Mexican restaurant that's close by. A good place to catch a bite after the theatre is John's Pizzeria also @ W. 44th. I would also recommend getting tickets to see Avenue Q, Dirty Rotten Scoundrels or Spamalot, we thoroughly enjoyed all of these shows. The TKTS booth is a great (safe/legit) place to get good seats at a discount (they accept cash only); for shows that are sold out try the theatre box office, most of the time a limited amount of SRO seats can be purchased for a fraction of the price as soon as the box office opens but be prepared to stand after walking around the city all day! Have a good stay in NYC!

<Author>Mauilovin
<Content>Perfect location, spectacular views We stayed here during the Thanksgiving holiday and were pleasantly surprised. We've stayed at other hotels in Manhattan, namely the Marriott and expected to be in cramped quarters or a glorified closet but this hotel is surprisingly lovely. My husband used his Starwood points so we stayed free. Our room was on the 39th floor overlooking the Hudson. This section is reserved for Starwood guests so I'm not sure if the other rooms are similiar but this room was fairly spacious (rare in NYC) and very modern. Check in was a breeze and the elevators with the headline news playing are a nice touch. Despite the holiday, valet service, and checkin were both extremely attentive and fast. The only issue- the foam pillows taking several hours to arrive in our room but the manager apologized and explained they were very busy. The best part of the trip was the surprisingly close access to the Macy's Day Parade. We were only one block away from the action and the crowd was very manageable, plus we could see the highlights on the big screen at TimesSquare. We were also within walking distance of all the great sites and the walk back to the hotel from The Color Purple on Broadway was quick and very romantic. This hotel is a great find on Broadway and we'd definitely stay here again. The only trouble we had was finding a cab, but that's to be expected in Manhattan.

<Author>memsdebby
<Content>Not up to Westin Standards - Not even close I just returned from a one night stay at the Westin in Times Square on November 25. I am usually a loyal Westin traveller and I chose this hotel because it is a Westin even though I have had mostly very positive experiences in NYC at other hotels. Things that I found lacking were: Location - They claim to be in Times square but they are really a full block off of the square. The hotel lobby is uninspired and is a full story above street level. Bell Service - No Bell hop arrived to help us unnload our car or valet park. I had to eventually go inside to find someone to give my keys to and ended up hauling the luggage out of the trunk myself with one of their carts. Also, getting my car out of the valet parking was a 45 minute ordeal once we were ready to leave. The parking rate is $45.00/day which is higher than many comparable hotels. Escalators/Eelvators - The main lobby escalator was broken during both days of our stay. Elderly people were having to struggle with their luggage down the broken escalator with a line of people pressing them from behind. There was a separate elevator to use but it was not clearly marked and no one knew where to find it. Also, I overheard one woman say that the upper floor elevators were malfunctioning and that it had taken her family 1 1/2 hours to get downstairs on Saturday morning because they could not get an elevator - even after calling the front desk to complain. There were many irritated people milling about the bell stand. Our room was not ready at the 3pm check-in. They told us to come back at 4:15. We ended up waiting in the lobby for about an hour. They gave us a free drink coupon for the bar which was closed so we never got to use it. They also tried the old smoking/non-smoking bait and switch. I reserved a non-smoking room but even with my confirmation number they still tried to put me in a smoking room. The room included complimentary breakfast and appetizers but the appetizers did not begin until 6pm. This makes it impossible for anyone to get any use out of this feature if they are attending the theatre unless they don't want dinner first. Also, the room was very crowded and dirty and there was no place to sit with your food. The beds were nice as usual. I am really not usually a complainer but I resent paying $450 per night to get treated this way. I know this is not typical of Westins and I know it was a holiday weekend, but I will not stay there again. For my money, I will stay at the Marriot Marquis, or even the Courtyard for goodness sakes. I hope they get their act together.

<Content>Spectacular views and location from the Westin NY We stayed at the Westin New York at Times Square in August 2005 for our Honeymoon in New York. The hotel is one block away from Times Sqaure and in the other direction one block away from the Broadway shows, all in all a fantastic location. Upon arrival we were greeted from the Taxi by Westin Staff with a smile, they collected our bags from the car and took our name to get them sent to the room, we were then able to check in without the hassle of luggage. The bags arrived in our room a couple of minutes after us. When we went to check in we were again greeted by friendly staff who upon finding out it was our honeymoon promised to move us to a corner room the next day for the remainder of our holiday - which was done. I have to say both rooms were spacious, clean and had spectacular views and I would have been happy staying in either room, although the corner room gave you a better landscape of New York and was overlooking the Hudson and the Statue of Liberty.The bed was extremely comfortable and the shower nice and powerful, although the bath is not as comfortable as you would hope for with the description given on the web - minor problems though. We were also able to get tickets to see The Producers from the Hotel ticket desk 2 days after arriving in New York - which saved queuing for hours in Times Square. As with any hotel the bar is outrageously expensive, but with New York on your doorstep who needs it. I thoroughly enjoyed my stay at the Westin and New York and would recommend it to others.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>We had a great time We loved our stay at the Westin. We were in New York from July 3rd to 10th for our honeymoon. We do not have any faults with the hotel at all only that the escalators to reception were broken a lot.The hotel is not a long walk away from Times Square as previous reviews have claimed it is simply just around the corner, we are really pleased we chose this hotel as we thought the location was perfect. Our rooms were cleaned every day and towels and toiletries were also replaced daily. The elevators are the fastest I have ever been in, so fast that you are dizzy when you get out of them.You must visit a restaraunt called Bubba Gump Shrimp which is in Times Square, the food is gorgeous (mainly Shrimp) and it's a really fun place to eat. We ate there a few times and I really miss it now I am back home in England.The Bell Boys are really helpfull also, we had a late flight so we stored our cases at no extra charge other than a tip and they also organised a town car for our trip back to the airport so we travelled in a bit more comfort than a yellow cab. We recomend that you use the town cars as they don't cost much more that a regular cab and they are more luxurious. Overall we loved our honeymoon in New York and although we were there a week we still did not see everything so we are definately planning on returning and are definately going to stay at the Westin.

We could see the Statue of Liberty from sitting in bed! and also the Sea, Air and Space Museum and the Empire State Building! The room was very spacious and clean as was the bathroom. Don't be put off by bad reviews as we couldn't fault the hotel or staff and if we ever come to New York again we wouldn't hesitate to use the Westin. :o)

We were out late at night around the hotel and felt very safe. <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not fantastic, but very nice indeed I liked this hotel. But be warned: it's not really at Times Square, it's at the end of a long street leading to it. So, if you're out at night, you're best to take a cab back. Having said that, it's worth the extra effort to stay there.My first night I did not get my confirmed room...I was given one that had just been put back into service...so it had no blinds, and I had to sleep on a fold out bed. Awful night's sleep. Awful.They made up for it the next 3 nights with a beautiful corner room with king size bed. Fantastic. Nice robe, good layout, very quiet, I could go on all day about the Westin Heavenly bed...I ate at the hotel restaurant almost every morning for breakfast. Fantastic service, great food. There is also very good security - after a certain hour you have to show your room card just to get into the lobby - I liked that. There is no pool, but there is a small work out room that was very well equipped. I used it for one day, but please note you are charged extra (there is a reduced fee if you want to use it for a week).The one thing really lacking about this hotel is housekeeping. No matter what I called them for - they just could not get it right. My first turn-down request was ignored completely. When i called the second night (at 6 p.m.), they told me no problem - then called back to say none was available. I'm doing somebody a favour by writing this - but don't use the phone. One 15 second phone call to L.A. where I said Hi, it's me. I'm in room 1412, call me back cost me $23.00....I imagine that's common pricing among big chain hotels in the Big Apple (it's also happened to me in L.A.), but still - it's ridiculous. Use your cell.I would stay there again. The convention I attended was at the Marriott and that really was located at Times Square - but it was a mess. Three or four escalators just to get to the lobby - and half the elevators weren't working. Fantastic view from the top of the Marriott's revolving restaurant but only go if you're on business - there's an expensive cover charge just to get a drink (I think it was $9.00 per person plus your order. They only waive it if you're staying there).If you expect pretty good service and a comfortable bed, you won't go wrong here.Regards,GT

The starting point for the NY Tours double decker bus line is just down the street from the hotel. <Content>Not totally wowed, but you could do a lot worse For our mini-getaway, we were lucky enough to secure an executive club corner room which was astoundingly spacious (especially for a NYC hotel) and very airy because of the 3 large windows which extend to almost the baseboard. Judging from the Westin web site, this particular style of window -- which ends in a rather narrow, suede-cushioned window seat -- is available only in the club level rooms, but the windows in any of the rooms here can be opened somewhat, a feature I always like.Our room furnishings (which included a chair and a sofa) were spotless  comfortable; the bed was almost as heavenly as their advertising would have you believe; the Bose CD/clock-radio was an unexpected bonus; and our bathroom was large, but had little shelf space  no other storage for toiletries. You too might find the 3 drawers in the desk area (the only ones provided for clothing) to be a bit skimpy, but the hallway closet -- amply stocked with good hangers -- handled our overflow.Apart from the terrific room, the club amenities were disappointing. As others here have commented, it is not a soothing atmosphere (two large-screen TV's were always on  the space is undersized for the number of people who have access to it), breakfast was ho-hum (please don't judge NYC bagels by the ones they have on hand) and the offerings for the evening cocktail hour were surprisingly limited: soda, red wine, white wine were the only beverages, and there were no snacks, just a pasta dish of some sort. We also noticed that the room service dishes of our neighbors languished in the hallway for longer than you might expect to see them.Although we heard more street traffic than we wanted (our room was on the 12th floor fronting 42nd Street), we heard no noise from any of our neighbors. The elevator service is superior to that of the Marriott Marquis, and because the Westin's atrium doesn't go all the way down to the meeting floors/lobby, there is not the attendant din as at the Marriott. Indeed, the Westin is more of an oasis in general than the Marquis from the congestion and sensory overload of Times Square... and it is a more pleasant  distinctive hotel than, e.g., the Hilton.Although I doubt we will rush to return here, I think this Westin would be a good choice for those who are visting New York to see the sights  who want a big city hotel experience.

<Author>cruisingonceagain
<Content>Excellent choice in New York!!! We just returned from a two-night stay at the Westin New York at Times Square. We had a fabulous view of Times Square - we were on the 43rd floor - and we had a deluxe double. The elevators in this hotel are very, very fast, and they have a TV in the elevators to entertain you during the short trip. There was never a wait for the elevators. The location is excellent - corner of 43rd and 8th Avenue. Right across is a Ben  Jerry's, and in the corner is Europan, a decent place for breakfast. We walked everywhere; everything is accessible. On one occasion, we took a cab to the American Museum of Natural History (Central Park West) and it was only $6.50. We decided to walk back so we could stroll along 5th Avenue and do some shopping. We walked to the United Nations but that is a quite a walk, but not bad. This is an excellent location if you love the theater (we do!). We even found reasonable parking on 43rd and 10th Avenue - $18 per 24 hours (look for parking in NYC in iconparking.com)! We will definitely stay here again. Highly recommened.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Clean, Comfortable, Modern My husband and I stayed in the Westin NY in February 2005 for one night and were very impressed. We love Westins in general... with the Heavenly beds and baths. This particular hotel was newly renovated and very clean. The bed was great with down blankets, pillows and crisp white sheets. The bath provides excellent elbow room for showers with double shower heads (one on top of the other - great for two people). We were on the 32? floor so we had a great view of the river. The location was perfect, only a block or two from Times Square. Room includes starbucks coffee and a flat screen tv, definitely a plus. The bathroom has a sliding glass door (a fogged look) that doesn't give much sound proofing, so you must be comfortable with your roommate :) I woke up a few times through the night because of the hallway sounds (doors slamming and people coming out of the elevator at 4am), but I suppose you could get that anywhere. We had drinks at the bar in the hotel that night, expensive but not terrible for the city ($12-$14 per drink). Sushi was good. We ate breakfast at Don Shulo's restaurant and it was EXCELLENT but extremely overpriced. We had eggs benedict, a belgian waffle and orange juice and paid $50+. They ask you if you want orange juice while holding the pitcher above your glass and they charge $6 for a small glass. The juice was 50% pulp, but thankfully we don't mind pulp. I would definitely stay there again, it's a 4-5 star place, great for a special occasion in the city. (Special occasion because it is expensive: we paid $250/night) If you don't stay at this Westin... stay at another one somewhere else... there are locations all over the world.

<Author>MGMarch
<Content>Pricey, but worth it Yes it's on the expensive side, but what nice hotel isn't in New York?Stayed Sat-Tue Easter weekend and had a very good experience. Had to work hard to get the price I got ($279/nt club level). Originally booked a non-club level room with two double beds for $329/nt Sun-Wed. Later I saw on Westin website they offered a 15% discount if checking in Thu-Sat. The webiste showed a club-level room at $279 with discount, but I was concerned about getting my desired double room (one person at Westin reservations said there was no guarantee). So I called the hotel directly and was told to book the room online and call back to get the two doubles guaranteed (traveling with wife and 2 teens). Everything worked out fine.We drove to New York, staying just outside of the city in Fairfield, NJ, so we could get into Manhattan early Saturday and start sightseeing. Our room was not available, but the desk agent put a hold on our double, so we checked our bags and car and set of.When we returned at about 4 p.m., we were able to check in quickly. We were booked into a handicapped accessible room and forgot to change it at check-in. Good move: the extra wide walking area in rooms made it seem all the more spacious. No NYC claustrophobia here. The only bad thing about the room was the location: it was on 15th floor at the corner of 8th and 42nd with a spectacular view of the Port Authority terminal! The club level is located on the lower floors (10-16 I think), so I am not sure any of them has much of a view. The plus side of the club level is the complimentary continental breakfast and evening hors d'ouevres. Avoiding the typical $15 per person cost of breakfast was a great deal; and we combined a late lunch with the evening snacks to avoid a $150 pre-theater dinner. The down side (at least this particular weekend) was the crowds. There was a seemingly endless flood of people, which kept the staff struggling to keep up with the demand. Still, the food choices varied daily and if you were patient, you always got enough to eat.While the location of the hotel is very good, the entrance is on 8th Avenue, something I overlooked when booking. That puts you more toward the peep-show side of things, but still just a short walk to Times Square. We had the extra benefit of a major sideshow. While the kids were at a movie (at the conveniently adjoining Loews theater), half of the NYPD (at least 20 squad cars) ended up on 42nd St. just below our window. The best I could tell, they were chasing down guys selling counterfeit purses (I saw a load of them in the back of one squad car). It was quite a scene; if that kind of stuff makes you nervous, you should probably avoid NYC altogether, or at least Times Square.We are not particularly demanding hotel guests: we expect a clean room and quick service, and were more than satisfied. I heartily recommend the Westin.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very nice experience!!! March 18 - 24, 2004. Our first trip to NYC and our choice of WTS was excellent. Both rooms were excellent although the corner room had much more room to store bags, etc. The heavenly bed and bath were as advertised. <Author>nyeze
<Content>Loved it. By New York city standards, this hotel is outstanding. Staff are friendly, helpful and courteous. The rooms are big (by NY city standard). The beds are to die for -- their signature Heavenly bed is no misnomer. And bathroom is spotless. I travel to New York about 10 times a year and have tried various Manhattan hotels but this was by far the best experience -- even allowing for the fact that this wasn't a Priceline or Hotwire rate. Usually encounter one or two bad apples from the doorman, bellhop, front desk, room service, housekeeper. But not this time. Everyone was exceptionally helpful.Elevators are fast -- which may sound like a minor point until you experience 10-15 min waits with other high rise hotels.If I had to name some negatives: (1) the walls a little thin so hopefully your neighbors are respective and (2) the central air/heat system was a little noisy -- but have experienced much worse with other hotels. By a little noisy I mean it wasn't whisper quiet.If you're looking for good central location, bigger than avg rooms and overall service level that typical NY hotels don't or can't provide, I recommend the Westin.

Would be nice to find a hotel room in NY that is current in decor (i.e., not Park Avenue stuffy and fringed) but a bit less dark and cold. Not a bad stay...but for the money and with Westin's name, I expected a bit more specialness. I've stayed in much better in NY for a lot less. O.K. to stay here...but don't expect anything special but the amazing bed.

The Heavenly Bed is magnificient! Definitely made the room worth it. The Times Square location is misleading, there are no views of Times Square from the hotel, although it is merely a block away (building obstruction). The hotel is really close to 42nd street sub station, theater district and various tourist traps. If you book the Westin, get a corner room!

<Author>JustATraveling
<Content>Definately Stay Again My husband, in-laws, brother-in-law, and I stayed at the Westin for a long weekend, last weekend. This is an excellent location. You can walk out the door, up half a block and be in the middle of Times Square. There are two subway stations a half a block, each way from the hotel. Plenty of places to eat even if you decide not to venture out....John's Pizza is outstanding, Carmine's (family-style Italian), Westway Deli (great cheesecake, cheaper breakfast, lunch and dinner). You can walk out your door, across the street to go see the Broadway production of The Lion King. The staff was very courteous. The conceirge managed to get us reservations for breakfast at Norma's in the Le Meridian Hotel. (A little pricy, but a must!) There is a movie theatre next door if you have to entertain children. I would highly recommend this hotel. It is comparable to the Hilton Times Square just a few doors up. We have stayed at both and would visit both again.

The double room we reserved was nice, but a little small. The light made it difficult for anyone to use in the middle of the night. The Hotel's beds are as advertised: phenomenal! The great selling point about the Hotel is the location and adjacent entertainment (BB King Blues Club downstairs, Shulas Steak House directly in front of the lobby, within the Hotel, great Bar Lounge. All in all a Wonderful Westin stay. Added note, NO traffic noise from the streets below.

I did a lot of research on various sites and deducted that the hotel was probably the Westin at Times Square. I had never used Hotwire before but decided to give it a try, and boy am I glad I did. I purchased the hotel room for half the price of what I was going to pay for a comprable room. <Author>twoworlds
<Content>Excellent Undoubtedly I got lucky with a corner room, but the Westin hotel was fantastic in so many ways. First and foremost, (and all too rare these days) there's a staff that is helpful, courteous, and actually knowledgable. Check in was a breeze. The room was great, with gorgeous views, and of course the Heavenly beds. After a full day walking the streets of New York for miles on end, sinking into those cool, crisp sheets on the soft bed truly was Heaven! We got large bottles of complimentary water each day. We were up high, but there was absolutely no street or traffic noise in our room. The bathroom was huge by New York standards, with large windows giving it a sense of even more space, (and an incredible view) and a double headed shower of my dreams!I would normally elect to stay anywhere BUT Times Square, but had no choice this time because the city was booked out. I honestly thought I was taking a risk with this hotel and was expecting to be disappointed. After literally hours of internet research this is not the place I would have chosen, so I was delighted to find it excelled in every way.The hotel is actually a block away from Times Square, so it is no as frenetic as being on the square, although being close everything is available within 50 feet! The price was good, the service was good, no complaints at all. I will definitely stay here next time, and I'll forget spending any more hours of research trying to find any place to beat it. What I like about this hotel as opposed to a W, is that this is new and modern, with clean/simple design, but not too cool for us ordinary folk.PS: When we were leaving for the airport, we had 1/2 hour to spare and needed to eat. We popped into Bar 10 downstairs and shared a foot long coney island pretzel dog. Something I had never heard of, a big ole hotdog wrapped in a pretzel. It sounded kind of dodgy to me but it was the quickest thing to order for 2 starving people - and OH MY! All I can say is that thing was soooo delicious, it was a good thing I was leaving or I would have been down there eating a hot dog for dinner every day. Try it with a glass of red; one of the best meals I've had all year...........

<Author>dshaver
<Content>Nice hotel but I expected more for the price -- I left just satisfied. My wife and I stayed here for three nights over a weekend in September 2004. I booked on Westin web site and paid an average of $220/night for a large, 11th floor, club level, corner room. While we did not have a view of the city, the room was very spacious by NYC standards. Overall we had a nice experience at the Westin, but it did not knock our socks off. If I had paid the $330/night rate rather than the 3-for-2 rate, I'd be way less happy.In general I'd say the staff was friendly and helpful but did not go out of their way to help make the stay special. Concierges were good and had great advice. Location was great -- close to Times Square and Theaters. Dream bed/shower were very nice. Overall, a good stay, but it seemed like we should have gotten more out of the hotel given the price.What that summary out of the way, here are a few more details.I'm a pretty frequent business traveller; about 100 nights a year in hotels. On an average trip I'm not very picky about hotels; I use these items to judge the quality/performance of the hotel experience against the price:1) Quiet room; Westin gets an A+ grade; no major noise from other guests2) Ability to control the room temperature; A+; great system3) Comfortable bed; A++++; Dream Bed was awesome4) Working space for laptop with reasonable access to phone, power, and Internet connection; grade A; great workspace and nice chair. I was unhappy with the $15/night for Internet fee, however.See? I told you I'm easy. :-)Much further down the list in my performance considerations:5) Competency and friendliness of staff; A6) Speed of check-in and check-out; A+; very fast7) Quality of food/beer either in hotel or nearby; A+; come on, it's Times Square -- you can find anything and it is all good!8) Lack of stupid charges like in room safe, extra fee for phone calls over 20 mins, etc; grade C; high costs for Internet and phone calls. I mean, really, $1.75 for a single 2 minute phone call to an 800 number? They also put a parking fee of $45/night on my room even though I did not have a car. Mistake or revenue enhancement? I don't know...With all of those performance criteria in mind, I measure price. You can tell that the Westin gets a solid A or maybe even an A+ in my mind -- great hotel, staff, etc. But measured against price, I'm a bit more reserved. Hotels in NYC are expensive and thus my expectations are very high. If I had same experience and quality of staff in Des Moines or Austin, I would have been raving. However, in NYC (at $220/night) I went away just satisfied.Bottom line: Stay here if you like the location and based on price you think Westin is being competitive. Said another way, don't over pay expecting an incredible experience.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Not mind-blowing, but ok... Just back after a 6 day stay at the Westin NY Times Square. First things first: if you really want to be in Times Square, this hotel is perfectly located. And make sure you have a room on higher levels (as from level 23) so you'll be able to enjoy a silent night. The problem with the Westin is that I booked it as being a tourist, while the hotel is all corporate. The people working there, the rooms, the public spaces: it's business all around. (also meaning: everything is extra,extra, extra. One rip-off exemple is the internet access; it's 14.95 $ for 24-hours...but they don't make it clear that for them, 24-hours start at 12 noon...). The room decoration lacks inspiration; I had a junior suite which offers sufficient space, although the bathroom is BIG, there is only one sink and the bath is made for SMALL people). Staff (especially bell men) are not too friendly, but hey this is NYC. All in all, if you really have/want/need to stay at Times Square and you want a clean, well-equipped room, than the Westin is a good choice. If not, for the money paid, there are a dozen better options available off Times Square...

Also, they promote late checkout, but we were told 1pm (sunday) was the latest because they were busy that day.So, to wrap up. Some minor issues with the service, but if you are looking for a great place to stay while enjoying New York, then take my advice and look no further.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Hotel and Location We just returned from a long weekend (6/25-2/28) from New York City. Our stay at the Westin was great. We arrived late Friday night, so we were unable to upgrade to better a room (clubroom or higher floor), but did get a corner room on the 19th floor. Check-in was easy and short, and everyone at the front desk was very helpful. The room was a little larger than the non-corner rooms, (since we had a short hallway to the bedroom area), and had plenty of windows (4 large windows) to view the city. Even on the 19th floor, we had some nice views. The room was a typical (clean and neat) Westin style (heavenly bed/bath) room and the room was always cleaned before 5pm each day. (Remember, there are over 800 rooms to be cleaned each day, and unless you leave real early in the morning, it may take all day before they can get to your room)We ate at Shula's for dinner one night and highly recommend it for meat lovers. The prices are high, typical plate is $40, but it is well worth it. You do have to pay for the side dishes, but they are very large and could easily feed 2-3 people. For dessert, try the chocolate cake with warm chocolate filling. The location of the hotel is great. Yes, it is not right on Times Square, but only a block or two away, a quick 5 minute walk. There are advantages of it not being on Times Square, particularly on a weekend night since it is almost wall to wall people on the sidewalks and would make it difficult to get to the entrance to your hotel. There are two movie theaters (Lowes and AMC), 2 Starbucks, a Yankees store, Cold Stone Creamery, McDonalds, and several other restaurants all within a blk or less of the hotel entrances (dont forget about the back entrance). Now for the Pros/Cons of the hotel:Pros - great location, easy access to subways, theater district (2 blks away), restaurant row (2 blks away), off the busy street of Times Square, friendly and courtesy staff, will give you umbrellas if it rains (at no cost to you), and the Heavenly Bed and BathCons - we can't think of one, since the hotel met or exceeded our expectationsWe would recommend this hotel to our family and friends.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>"Trendy" Westin quality in NYC The Times Square Westin lives up to the Westin quality that you would expect. While the hotel is not as classic and formal as you would find most Westin hotels, the Times Square Westin certainly distinguishes itself from average (and most above-average) hotels. Overall, the hotel is extremely neat, modern, and clean. The style is quite modern, and totally fits in with it's proximity to Times Square, Broadway, etc... We booked our stay in a standard guestroom through the Starwood website, and secured our 10% AAA discount (they also had a number of package deals available online). At a rate of $179/nite - on the weekend - anyone would (or should) be hard-pressed to find problems with the Westin. Our stay was no exception. We had to wait about 5 min. for a room. Apparently, another room was found for us in the meantime. A room on the southwest corner of the 42nd floor - what a spectacular view !! Understandably, your comfort with how much you pay for a room at this hotel will depend upon your room location (i.e., a side-street room on the 11th floor is not quite as exciting at night).Regardless of the room location, the room was clean, modern, and really stylish. Of course, the heavenly bed and heavenly shower make the Westin rooms complete!The location of the hotel is completely convenient to Times Square, and we didn't feel unsafe on our walk back to the hotel late at night.We'll certainly stay at the Times Square Westin again, and we recommend the hotel to anyone interested in a great value - a very nice hotel in a great location, at a reasonable price!

<Author>ima_gypsy
<Content>Great hotel ! I thought the hotel itself was fabulous. I had a corner room on a high floor with lots of windows and great views, plus it had the most wonderful large bathroom *with a window* and a great view. The decor was sleekly modern without being cold. The beds were typically Westin plush and very very comfortable. I felt very very comfortable in the room and was happy to return to it at the end of each day. I had excellent room service breakfasts, perfectly prepared, and the front desk staff were the best ! The common areas and bar/restuarant also looked great, though I did not check out the latter.However, I did check out early and escaped to another hotel. My room overlooked a large rooftop terrace on an apartment or condo building across the street (43rd Street, I guess), and a horribly loud party fired up one night complete with window rattling (literally) booming bass, so horrible that I requested to switch rooms. The hotel was fully booked and there was no available room for me to move to. The desk staff and management were extremely helpful and polite throughout this ordeal and helped me find another hotel to move to.Staying right in Times Square was a bit of a pain. Aside from the unusual party, my room was very very quiet and insulated from the noise on the streets below. But walking around in the Times Square area was annoying. It's just not the area for me .. too many tourists, too many chain restaurants, too much junk. (I'm used to staying on hotels surrounding Central Park). But that's just Times Square and has nothing to do with the hotel. If you have the need or wish to stay in that area, then by all means stay at the Westin !So overall I highly recommend this hotel even though I'll admit I'm unlikely to return to it because of the Times Square location.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Heavenly! Free Upgrade Too! I couldn't agree more with the reviewer from Cambridge. I've experienced NYC's trendy new boutique hotels that offer you a closet to sleep in and a bar that will be out of style before I finish this review. Now, they have their good points, mind you...but as a (ahem) card-carrying member of Generation Y, I'm confident the Westin will withstand the test of time; it's light-years ahead of the tragically hip hostelries that fancy themselves too cool for a sign at the front door. I'm beginning to think Hudson has resorted to hiring its twentysomething staffers to use the hallways as make-out spots more often these days, just for atmosphere Eh, whatever. If you ever need my help cleaning those, er, white stains on the carpet I found on the way past Lover's Lane(...sigh...), you'll find me at the Westin. I'll be luxuriating on a massive Heavenly Bed, snacking on a scrumptious filet from Shula's steak house (yes, Don Shula), gazing out at Times Square from an architectural masterpiece - for less money than Hudson, Paramount, Morgans or Royalton. I wish I could have found an excellent promotional rate for my first stay this past Christmas, but my $219 got me a complimentary surprise upgrade to a 9th floor Club Level corner room with a view of 42nd street, including complimentary continental breakfast. The decor is modern and tasteful, but the larger rooms aren't very well lit. THE BEDS ARE AMAZING! I was skeptical when I heard about the Heavenly Bed thing, but seriously, folks - this was the first time I slept through a wake-up call in a hotel. The staff was cordial and professional, especially our bellman, although the valet parking leaves something to be desired. Try to secure a rate that includes parking, especially around the holidays. All in all, I'd return to the Westin in a New York minute. This place really is a shot of Tequila in the arm of traditional New York...and not a white stain in, uh, sight.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>mixed- great views, nice gym Everyone on the staff at this hotel is extremely pleasant and polite, which is a real plus, however, some were not at all knowledgeable about basic functions at the hotel. I had a corner room on a high floor. It was not large, but had a spectacular view of the Hudson River and the Empire State Building, which neutralized the remarkably unattractive decor of the room. The bed was comfortable and the room was functional. The bathroom was cavernous and cold, but the great view helped to balance this and make it more pleasant. There were too many minor annoyances for a hotel this price- phone not connected, iron malfunctioned, shower curtain dirty, to name a few. Also, the hotel nickel-and-dimes you, with charges for the gym and by providing only one free coffee in your room (if you want more, you have to buy it from the mini-bar). The gym is well-equipped, spacious and has a nice view. If this hotel were less expensive, the negatives would be less important. If they would brighten up the decor, warm up the bathroom, drop the gym charge and be less stingy with the coffee, I would make this my regular NY hotel. The other annoyance is that they refuse to guarantee a specific type of room until you check in, which is unacceptable to me.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Westin Nice but Amenities Costly New York City's new Westin at Time's Square certainly is one sleek, modern hotel. This 4-star hotel presents itself admirably on first sight, and you won't be disappointed once inside. It's clean, ultra-modern rooms are nicely sized and decorated in a black/gray/white/chrome color scheme. My partner and I were in NYC for three overnights from August 26 to 29, 2003, and our stay at the Westin made coming back to the hotel at the end of the day a comfortable experience. Most room amenities were very nice including the Heavenly bed which was wonderful to sleep on. The Heavenly bath was good too. I opted for the tub, which was no better than your own home bathroom, so no big praise there. However, my partner greatly enjoyed the two-headed shower which was very soothing to sore muscles. We both wondered what was up with the 'Heavenly bath products' they advertised as available with the room. Yes, you could BUY Heavenly bath products from their hotel store, but the only bath products available were the standard small hotel-sized shampoo, conditioner and lotion you get in almost any hotel. We had two other MAJOR 'amenity' disappointments with this stay, which may have been because of our own lack of experience with how some hotels price things. Before booking this hotel, I thoroughly researched this and other hotels in its caliber, and several amenities were listed as though included in the cost of the room. For instance, high-speed internet access is listed as a room amenity, and we assumed, when booking, that this was available as part of the room cost. This was not so#8212;the cost was $14.95 per DAY for Internet access. For a few days stay and the need to connect, you end up paying as much as you do for your entire MONTH'S home cable internet connection costs. Another 'amenity' that we believed was included with the room was the Fitness Center. We came with our workout clothes ready to enjoy the Fitness Center, but discovered that to use it would cost an additional $10.00 per PERSON per day. We thought that cost was outrageous considering the cost of the room coupled with other already-high amenity charges. As far as staff was concerned, they were wonderfully courteous, friendly and professional. However, one evening we asked the concierge for recommendations for a 'great French restaurant'. We were referred to two French restaurants which, upon checking their menus, displayed more American dishes than French. We also had asked the concierge his opinion about 'restaurant row' (found on 46th street) where numerous French and other restaurants can be found, and the concierge stated he would not recommend any of those. Well, my partner is a European who has traveled, stayed and dined extensively all over France, and we ended up at Le Rivage on restaurant row and enjoyed a delicious authentic French meal! So much for the concierge knowledge and recommendation in that case! But, all in all, our stay was quite comfortable. We just wish the Westin Hotel didn't need to nickel-and-dime you for many of the amenity costs which they appear to advertise as included with the room. If you are aware of this and it's okay, then you won't otherwise be disappointed with this hotel. Would we stay there again? We would probably choose the Doubletree Guest Suites which are just as nice AND with lower amenity charges.

<Content>4 days at the NY Westin Stayed at the NY Westin Times Square 8/8-8/11. It was a wonderful Hotel. Very close to Times Square/Theatre Dist. The room was not as small as I had expected from reading other reviews. The shower head was great! The sink and counter space in the bathroom was very limited for most women's things. The bed was very comfortable, couldnt get the room cold enough for all of the down blankets on bed. After checking out and leaving my husband realized he left his wallet in the safe. We called security and they checked the room 2x and found it, Fed Ex'd to us right off. Our friends in another room also left things, the maid had found them and returned them. The Hotel does not call you if they find things left behind, they put it in lost and found and leave it to you call. Overall it was a great stay, hotel was quiet and you can get away from the noise in Times Square. I'm sorry to say we did not make it to the SPA. We did eat at Shula's, it seemed expensive compared to other restaurants in the area. I would stay here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Simply Perfect I travel regularly to New York...and the westin times square was by FAR the BEST hotel I've stayed in! The staff was very friendly and did everything they could to make my trip absolutely perfect. When i was checking in...I was upgraded to a BEAUTIFUL corner room..so I had windows almost all the way around the room. It had a nice view of the city. The next time i got to NY..i plan on staying at the westin again! After being there and talking with the great staff... I wouldnt stay anywhere else!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>What a "Heavenly" Hotel We booked the trip through Hotwire.com...paid $1100 for 4 nights hotel and direct flights to and from. Stayed from 7/23/2003 - 7/27/2003.Check-in was a snap, but probably due to the fact that we didn't arrive until 11:00pm. During the day long lines did develop at the huge front desk with only 1 or 2 people working. We had requested a corner room on one of the upper floors with a city view, but by the time we arrived they only had 7 rooms left so they upgraded us to a Deluxe room instead of the Superior room. WOW! The room was huge and extremely clean and we had a decent view from the 16th floor. You hear horror stories of how small the rooms can be in NYC, but not this room. The bathroom had plenty of space and enough towels to dry half of Times Sqaure!And for all the Heavenly amenities...well I now know why they call them Heavenly. The shower felt like you were standing in a waterfall, and the bed was THE best bed I have ever slept on....and if your in NYC on vacation and plan on doing a lot of walking like we did...then the Heavenly Shower/Bed is the best remedy for tired legs!The maid service was excellent and the security was very nice at the front door (they have a sign posted you must present your room key to enter but they never once asked to see our key). The hotel was very quite at night...but if you like to sounds of NYC at night just crack the windows open a little.All in all...great hotel with great service (for what we needed) in a great location. I will have a hard time staying anywhere else on my next trip to NYC.
